Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Shuf'ah and Subsidiary Sale in Dower with Return Payment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shuf'ah in dower with return condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on shuf'ah in a house given as dower with a condition to return money, and explain why Abu Hanifa considers the sale subsidiary.

Core Idea
When sale is subsidiary to marriage, it does not trigger shuf'ah, even though money is exchanged.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a pre-emption right (shuf'ah) arises when a house is given as dower (mahr) with a condition that the wife returns a sum of money to the husband. Both Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples agree that pure dower houses do not give shuf'ah, but they differ when a monetary return is stipulated. Understanding their reasoning deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists classify transactions and apply the principle that subsidiary matters follow the primary ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario and the legal issue
Read the case: a man marries a woman, gives her a house as dower, but stipulates that she must return 1000 dirhams to him. The question is whether any co-owner of the house can claim shuf'ah if the house is later sold or transferred.
The dispute is only about shuf'ah; there is no dispute on the validity of the marriage or the condition.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his primary argument
Abu Hanifa rules that no shuf'ah exists in any part of the house. His central argument: the sale aspect here is subsidiary (tabi‘) to the marriage contract. He supports this with two points: the transaction is concluded with marriage words (nikah) and it is not invalidated by a condition of marriage.
The subsidiary nature means that the legal effects of a primary sale (like shuf'ah) do not apply.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their counter-argument
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn) hold that shuf'ah applies in the portion of the house equivalent to the amount of money returned. They see the transaction as having two components: part of the house is dower (no shuf'ah) and part is a sale of the house for the money (shuf'ah applies). They consider the return of money as a monetary exchange (mubadalah maliyyah) that is primary in that part.
For the Sahibayn, the presence of a monetary exchange, even within a marriage, can generate shuf'ah if it is sufficiently independent.
4
Analyze the key point of contention: subsidiary vs. primary
The core disagreement lies in how to characterize the transaction. Abu Hanifa views it as a single transaction where marriage is intended (maqsud) and sale is incidental; the Sahibayn view it as two separate transactions. The text clarifies Abu Hanifa's reasoning by analogy: just as a mudarib's profit is subsidiary to the principal and does not give the capital owner shuf'ah, here the sale is subsidiary to marriage.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is clear: under Abu Hanifa, no shuf'ah; under the Sahibayn, shuf'ah exists in the part of the house equal to the returned money.

ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال اس بیع کا لفظ نکاح سے منعقد ہو جانا اس بات کی کھلی دلیل ہے کہ بیع یہاں تابع ہے اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ بیع شروط فاسدہ سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ مگر نکاح شروط فاسدہ سے فاسد نہیں ہو گا۔ اگر اس کو بیع شمار کیا جائے تو پھر بیچ کے اندر نکاح کی شرط لگانا شرط فاسد ہے جس سے بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ بیع شرط نکاح سے فاسد نہیں ہو رہی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بیچ یہاں تابع ہے۔
And if he married her on [condition of giving] a house on the condition that she would return a thousand to him, then there is no shuf'ah in the entire house according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: shuf'ah is due in the share of the thousand, because it is a monetary exchange regarding him. And he (Abu Hanifa) says: the meaning of sale in it is subsidiary, and for this reason it is concluded with the word of marriage and is not invalidated by the condition of marriage in it. And there is no shuf'ah in the original (marriage), so likewise in the subsidiary. And because shuf'ah is legislated for monetary exchange that is intended. Even that when a mudarib sells a house and there is profit in it, the owner of capital does not deserve shuf'ah in the share of the profit because it is subsidiary in it. Translation: And if he married a woman on a house on the condition that she would return to him a thousand dirhams, then according to Abu Hanifa there is no shuf'ah in any part of the house. And the Sahibayn said: shuf'ah will apply in the portion of the thousand, because it is a monetary exchange on his part (the husband's side). And Abu Hanifa says: the meaning of sale in this is subsidiary, and for this reason this sale is concluded with the word of marriage and is not invalidated by the condition of marriage in it. And there is no shuf'ah in the original (marriage), so likewise in the subsidiary. And because shuf'ah is legislated for monetary exchange that is intended. To the extent that when a mudarib sells a house and there is profit in it, the owner of capital does not deserve shuf'ah in the share of the profit because it is subsidiary in it. Commentary: A person married a woman and fixed a house as dower, and also stipulated that the entire house would be given but the woman must return a thousand dirhams. In this case, is there shuf'ah or not? It has already passed in the previous section that according to the Hanafis, there is no shuf'ah in the house given as dower. But here there is some form of exchange, so Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differed. The Sahibayn said: It is agreed that there is no shuf'ah in the house given as dower, but here there are two aspects: (1) part of the house is given as dower (no shuf'ah) and (2) part of the house is sold for a thousand (shuf'ah applies). So we say that shuf'ah will apply in that portion equal to the thousand, because it is an exchange of property for property, in which shuf'ah occurs. Imam Abu Hanifa said: There will be no shuf'ah in any part of the house here. Question: Why is there no sale here? Answer: Here there is both sale and marriage, but marriage is the primary intention and the sale is merely subsidiary; therefore only the primary is considered and shuf'ah is not established. Question: Why is the sale here subsidiary? Answer: Because if the sale were the primary intention, it would not be concluded with the word of marriage, since it is valid to intend the effect by mentioning the cause, but not to intend the cause by mentioning the effect. A sale can conclude a marriage, but a marriage cannot conclude a sale. Liberation and emancipation can effect divorce, but divorce cannot establish emancipation. In any case, the fact that this sale is concluded with the word of marriage is clear evidence that the sale is subsidiary here. And it is also agreed that a sale is invalidated by invalid conditions, but a marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions. If this were considered a sale, then stipulating a condition of marriage in the sale would be an invalid condition that invalidates the sale. Yet this 'sale' is not invalidated by the condition of marriage, which also shows that the sale is subsidiary.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding whether shuf'ah exists when a house is given as dower with a condition that the wife returns a sum of money (1000 dirhams) to the husband. The Sahibayn argue that the transaction contains two elements: part of the house is dower (no shuf'ah) and part is effectively a sale of a portion of the house for 1000 dirhams (shuf'ah applies). They consider the return of money as a monetary exchange, which triggers shuf'ah in the portion equivalent to the money. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, rules that no shuf'ah applies to any part of the house. His reasoning: the sale aspect here is subsidiary (tabi') to the marriage contract. Evidence for this includes: (1) the transaction can be concluded with the word 'nikah' (marriage), which would not be possible if the sale were primary; (2) the transaction is not invalidated by a condition of marriage, whereas a pure sale would be invalidated by such a condition; (3) the principle that shuf'ah is only legislated for monetary exchanges that are intended (maqsudah) and not for subsidiary ones. The text analogizes to the mudarabah case: if a mudarib sells a house and makes a profit, the capital owner (rabb al-mal) does not have shuf'ah in the profit portion because the profit is subsidiary to the principal. The commentary (Urdu) elaborates on the arguments: the Sahibayn saw two separate transactions, while Abu Hanifa saw a single transaction where sale is subordinate. The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, no co-owner can claim shuf'ah; under the Sahibayn's view, a co-owner can claim shuf'ah in the portion of the house equal to the money returned.

Key Terms
تابع (tabi'): Subsidiary – the sale aspect is subordinate to the marriage contract
مبادلة مالية (mubadalah maliyyah): Monetary exchange – a transaction where property is exchanged for property; shuf'ah is established for such exchanges when they are intended (maqsudah)
مقصود (maqsud): Intended or primary – shuf'ah is only for monetary exchanges that are the primary purpose of the transaction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), why does shuf'ah apply in the portion of the house equal to the thousand dirhams?
A) Because the entire transaction is a sale and shuf'ah applies to all sales.
B) Because the return of money creates a monetary exchange that is intended in that part.
C) Because the marriage is invalid and therefore the house is sold.
D) Because the wife is the owner of the house and sells it to the husband.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the classification of a transaction as primary or subsidiary determines whether shuf'ah arises; when a sale is subsidiary to marriage, it does not trigger pre-emption rights according to Abu Hanifa.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Shuf'ah When Mahr Includes a Conditional Monetary Return: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shuf'ah in hybrid marriage-sale contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on shuf'ah in a marriage contract with a conditional monetary exchange, apply Abu Hanifa's reasoning based on the principle of tabi' (subordinate), and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When marriage is primary and sale subordinate, shuf'ah follows the primary — so no shuf'ah.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement about the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) in a marriage contract that includes a conditional monetary exchange. While the Sahibayn see a partial sale triggering shuf'ah, Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the sale aspect is entirely subordinate to marriage, and thus shuf'ah does not apply. The discussion reveals a key principle of Hanafi fiqh: the subordinate follows the primary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Scenario
A man marries a woman with a house as mahr on the condition that the woman returns 1000 dirhams to him. Identify the two elements: marriage and a conditional financial exchange.
The financial exchange is embedded in the marriage contract.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa: no shuf'ah in any part of the house. Sahibayn: shuf'ah applies to the portion equivalent to the 1000 returned, because that part is a sale.
Both views are from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Proof
The contract is concluded with the word 'nikah', not 'bay'. Sale is subordinate (tabi') to marriage. Since shuf'ah does not apply in marriage, it also does not apply in the subordinate sale. Also, marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions, but a sale would be — the fact that this transaction is not invalidated proves it is not an independent sale.
The subordination is proven by linguistic and legal arguments.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's Proof
They argue that the part of the house valued at 1000 is a pure financial exchange (mubadalah maliyyah), which is the basis for shuf'ah. The rest remains mahr without shuf'ah.
They split the transaction into two parts.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The text (Ashraf al-Hidaya) favors Abu Hanifa's view because the sale is clearly subordinate. An analogy is drawn from mudaraba: profit is subordinate to capital, so no shuf'ah in profit when the capital's agent sells.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

ما قبل میں یہ بات تو گذر چکی کہ حنفیہ کے نزدیک اس مکان میں شفعہ نہیں ہوتا جو مبر میں دیا گیا ہے۔ مگر یہاں کچھ تبادلہ کی شکل پائی گئی اس وجہ سے اس مسئلہ میں نام بوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہو گیا۔
صاحبین نے کہا کہ یہ مسئلہ تو مسلم ہے کہ مہر والے گھر میں شفعہ نہیں ہوتا مگر یہاں دو صورتیں ہیں۔
ان گھر کا کچھ حصہ گویا کہ شوہر نے مہر میں دیا ہے اور اس میں شفعہ نہیں ہوتا ۔
۲۔ اور گھر کا کچھ حصہ ہزار میں فروخت کیا ہے اور اس صورت میں شفعہ ہوا کرتا ہے۔ لہذا ہم نے کہا کہ اتنے حصہ میں شفعہ ہو گا۔ جہاں تک ہزار کی مالیت ہے اسلئے کہ یہ مبادلتہ المال بالمال ہے جس میں شفعہ ہوا کرتا ہے۔
امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ گھر کے کسی بھی حصہ میں یہاں شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔
سوال ... کیوں یہاں بیع تو ہے ہی نہیں؟
جواب یہاں بیج بھی ہے اور نکاح بھی ہے۔ مگر نکاح مقصود اصلی ہے اور بیچ تابع محض ہے اس وجہ سے صرف متبوع کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا اور شفعہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ سوال بیع یہاں تابع کیوں ہے؟
جواب ... اسلئے کہ اگر یہاں بیج ہی مقصود ہوتی تو پھر لفظ نکاح سے منعقد نہ ہوتی کیونکہ سبب بول کر مسبب تو مراد لینا درست ہے اور مسبب بول کر سبب مراد لینا درست نہیں۔ بیچ سے نکاح تو منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ مگر نکاح سے بیع منعقد نہیں ہوتی ۔ تحریر و اعتاق سے طلاق ہو جائے گی مگر طلاق سے عشق ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال اس بیع کا لفظ نکاح سے منعقد ہو جانا اس بات کی کھلی دلیل ہے کہ بیع یہاں تابع ہے اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ بیع شروط فاسدہ سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ مگر نکاح شروط فاسدہ سے فاسد نہیں ہو گا۔ اگر اس کو بیع شمار کیا جائے تو پھر بیچ کے اندر نکاح کی شرط لگانا شرط فاسد ہے جس سے بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ بیع شرط نکاح سے فاسد نہیں ہو رہی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بیچ یہاں تابع ہے۔
اس تقریر سے جب یہ بات معلوم ہو گئی کہ یہاں نکاح اصل اور بیع تابع ہے تو جب نکاح یعنی اصل کے اندر شفعہ نہیں ہے تو یہاں کی بیع میں جو تابع ہے شفعہ نہیں ہوگا۔ پھر دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ شفعہ اس مبادلہ مالی میں ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ جہاں مباکہ کالی مقصود ہو اور یہاں نکاح مقصود ہے نہ کہ مالی مبادلہ جیسا کہ تقریر مذکور سے معلوم ہوا ، کیا اس کی کوئی مثال پیش کر سکتے ہیں؟ جی ہاں رب المال نے مضارب کو ایک ہزار روپے تجارت کیلئے دیئے۔ اس نے تجارت کی اور ایک ہزار کا نفع ہوا۔ پھر مضارب نے دو ہزار میں ایک مکان خریدا۔ اب اس کو فروخت کر دیا۔ رب المال کو حق شفعہ پہنچتا تھا اس نے اس مکان میں شفعہ کا دعویٰ کر دیا تو کیا رب المال کو شفعہ ملے گا۔ جواب دیا کہ نہیں ملے گا۔ کیوں اسلئے کہ رب المال موکل کے درجہ میں ہے اور مضارب وکیل ہے اور وکیل کی بیع مؤکل کی بیع ہوتی ہے تو یہ تو ایسا ہو گیا کہ خود ہی مالک فروخت کرے اور خود ہی شفعہ کا دعوی کرے۔
سوال ... جو اس میں ہزار روپے کا نفع ہے اس میں تو مضارب کو وکیل اور رب الممال کو موکل نہ قرار دے کر نصف مکان جو نفع کے حصہ کا ہے رب المال کو اس میں شفعہ ملنا چاہئے؟
جواب نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ نفع یہاں مقصود نہیں بلکہ مقصود مال مضاربت ہے۔ بہر حال تابع کو یہاں متبوع کے درجہ میں رکھ کر شفعہ جاری نہیں کیا گیا اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں تابع یعنی بیع کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ متبوع یعنی نکاح کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔
And if a man marries a woman with a house on the condition that the woman returns to him one thousand rupees, then according to Abu Hanifa there is no shuf'ah in any part of the house. And the Sahibayn said that there will be shuf'ah in the portion of the thousand, because this is a financial exchange (from the husband's perspective). And Abu Hanifa says that in this, the meaning of sale is subordinate, and for that reason this sale is concluded with the word of marriage, and it is not invalidated by the condition of marriage, and the original (marriage) has no shuf'ah; similarly, the sale (which is subordinate) also has no shuf'ah. And shuf'ah is legislated in a financial exchange that is intended. Up to here: when the mudarib sold the house and there is profit in it, the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) will not be entitled to shuf'ah in the portion of the profit, due to the subordination of profit. Explanation: A person married a woman and specified a house as mahr, and along with it he also placed the condition that the entire house will be given as mahr, but the woman must return one thousand rupees to me. In this case, is there shuf'ah or not? It has passed that according to the Hanafis, there is no shuf'ah in a house given as mahr. But here a form of exchange is found, due to which there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. The Sahibayn said that it is agreed that there is no shuf'ah in the house that is mahr, but here there are two situations: (1) a part of the house is given as mahr by the husband, and in that there is no shuf'ah; (2) and a part of the house is sold for a thousand, and in that case shuf'ah occurs. So we said that there will be shuf'ah in that portion, as much as the value of a thousand, because this is an exchange of property for property, in which shuf'ah occurs. Imam Abu Hanifa said that no shuf'ah will be obtained in any part of the house here. Question: Why? Is there no sale here? Answer: Here there is both sale and marriage. But marriage is the primary purpose, and sale is merely subordinate; therefore, only the primary will be considered, and shuf'ah will not be established. Question: Why is the sale subordinate here? Answer: Because if sale were the purpose here, then it would not be concluded with the word of marriage, since it is correct to mean the effect by stating the cause, but it is not correct to mean the cause by stating the effect. Sale can conclude marriage, but marriage does not conclude sale. Manumission and emancipation can effect divorce, but divorce does not establish emancipation. In any case, the fact that this sale is concluded with the word of marriage is clear evidence that the sale here is subordinate. And it is also agreed that sale is invalidated by invalid conditions, but marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions. If this were considered a sale, then placing a marriage condition in a sale would be an invalid condition that invalidates the sale, whereas this sale is not invalidated by the condition of marriage. This also indicates that the sale is subordinate here. From this discussion, when it became known that here marriage is the original and sale is subordinate, then since there is no shuf'ah in the original (marriage), there will be no shuf'ah in the sale which is subordinate. Then another principle is that shuf'ah is established in a financial exchange where financial exchange is the purpose. And here marriage is the purpose, not financial exchange, as understood from the above discussion. Can we present an example of this? Yes: The owner of capital gave a mudarib one thousand rupees for trade. He traded and made a profit of one thousand. Then the mudarib bought a house for two thousand. Then he sold it. The owner of capital, who had a right of shuf'ah, claimed shuf'ah in this house. So will the owner of capital get shuf'ah? The answer is no, because the owner of capital is in the position of principal and the mudarib is agent, and the sale of the agent is the sale of the principal. So this would be as if the owner himself sold and himself claimed shuf'ah. Question: In this, there is a profit of one thousand rupees; why should the mudarib not be considered the agent and the owner the principal regarding the half of the house that is the share of profit, so that the owner should get shuf'ah in it? Answer: He will not get it because profit is not the purpose here; rather the purpose is the capital of mudaraba. In any case, the subordinate is not given the status of the primary in applying shuf'ah. Similarly, in the mentioned case, the subordinate (sale) is not considered; rather the primary (marriage) is considered.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of shuf'ah (pre-emption) when a house is given as mahr with a condition that the wife returns a sum of money. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider part of the transaction as a sale of a portion of the house, thus shuf'ah applies to that portion. Abu Hanifa, however, rules that no shuf'ah applies at all, because the sale is subordinate (tabi) to the marriage contract, and shuf'ah is not established in marriage. The commentary defends Abu Hanifa's view through several proofs: (1) The contract is concluded with the word 'nikah', not 'bay'; therefore, the sale is subordinate. (2) Marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions, whereas sale is. (3) Shuf'ah is legislated only in financial exchanges that are the primary purpose. The passage also provides an analogy from mudaraba to illustrate the principle that the subordinate follows the primary in rulings. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, as the text supports it with extensive reasoning.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption; the right to take over a sold property by paying its price to the buyer, established in the Hanafi school for co-owners or neighbors.
المبادلة المالية (al-mubadalah al-maliyyah): Financial exchange; a transaction where property is exchanged for property, considered primary for shuf'ah to apply.
تابع (tabi'): Subordinate; something that is not the primary purpose of the contract but follows it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is there no shuf'ah in the house when a man marries a woman with a house as mahr on condition she returns 1000 rupees?
A) Because the house is given as mahr, and mahr never gives shuf'ah.
B) Because there is no sale at all, only marriage.
C) Because the sale is subordinate to the marriage contract, and shuf'ah is not established in the subordinate.
D) Because the condition of returning money invalidates the marriage, so no shuf'ah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a sale is subordinate (tabi') to a marriage contract, shuf'ah does not apply because the primary purpose (marriage) lacks shuf'ah.

Shuf'ah Not Established in Subordinate Sales (Nikah and Mudaraba)
Ruling with proof: shuf'ah in subordinate sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why shuf'ah is not established in a sale that is subordinate to a non-financial contract and apply the principle to similar cases.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah requires a purely financial exchange; a subordinate sale does not trigger shuf'ah.

Shuf'ah (preemption) is a right that allows a co-owner or neighbor to step into the buyer's shoes in a property sale. However, this right is limited to pure financial transactions. When a sale is incidental to a non-financial primary contract like marriage (nikah) or an agency relationship like mudaraba, the sale's nature changes. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that in such cases, shuf'ah does not apply, using both a general principle and a concrete example from mudaraba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a sale that occurs as part of a marriage contract (e.g., selling a house as dower). The ruling is that shuf'ah is not established in such a sale because it is subordinate to nikah, which is not a financial contract.
The act is the sale itself, but its context determines the ruling.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites a general principle: shuf'ah is established only in a purely financial exchange (mubadala mali) where financial consideration is the primary object. This is supported by an analogy (qiyas) from mudaraba: when a mudarib sells property bought with capital, the owner cannot claim shuf'ah because the sale is attributed to the owner himself.
The mudaraba example serves as an illustrative qiyas to reinforce the principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
In the mudaraba example, the mudarib is an agent (wakil); his sale is legally the principal's sale. If the principal cannot claim shuf'ah against his own sale, the ruling is that no shuf'ah arises. Similarly, in nikah, the sale is not an independent financial transaction but a subordinate part of a marriage contract; therefore, it does not meet the condition of a pure financial exchange.
The analogy is based on the illa (effective cause): the primary objective is not financial.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
The passage does not detail a disagreement, but the Hanafi position is that shuf'ah is strictly limited. Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow shuf'ah in broader circumstances, but the Hanafi relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that no shuf'ah arises in subordinate sales.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader fiqh tradition.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi school adopts the view that shuf'ah is not established in such cases. This is based on the clear principle and sound analogy. The mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) is that no shuf'ah applies.
No explicit tarjih authority is mentioned, but the passage reflects the established zahir al-riwayah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس تقریر سے جب یہ بات معلوم ہو گئی کہ یہاں نکاح اصل اور بیع تابع ہے تو جب نکاح یعنی اصل کے اندر شفعہ نہیں ہے تو یہاں کی بیع میں جو تابع ہے شفعہ نہیں ہوگا۔ پھر دوسرا اصول یہ ہے کہ شفعہ اس مبادلہ مالی میں ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ جہاں مباکہ کالی مقصود ہو اور یہاں نکاح مقصود ہے نہ کہ مالی مبادلہ جیسا کہ تقریر مذکور سے معلوم ہوا ، کیا اس کی کوئی مثال پیش کر سکتے ہیں؟ جی ہاں رب المال نے مضارب کو ایک ہزار روپے تجارت کیلئے دیئے۔ اس نے تجارت کی اور ایک ہزار کا نفع ہوا۔ پھر مضارب نے دو ہزار میں ایک مکان خریدا۔ اب اس کو فروخت کر دیا۔ رب المال کو حق شفعہ پہنچتا تھا اس نے اس مکان میں شفعہ کا دعویٰ کر دیا تو کیا رب المال کو شفعہ ملے گا۔ جواب دیا کہ نہیں ملے گا۔ کیوں اسلئے کہ رب المال موکل کے درجہ میں ہے اور مضارب وکیل ہے اور وکیل کی بیع مؤکل کی بیع ہوتی ہے تو یہ تو ایسا ہو گیا کہ خود ہی مالک فروخت کرے اور خود ہی شفعہ کا دعوی کرے۔ سوال ... جو اس میں ہزار روپے کا نفع ہے اس میں تو مضارب کو وکیل اور رب الممال کو موکل نہ قرار دے کر نصف مکان جو نفع کے حصہ کا ہے رب المال کو اس میں شفعہ ملنا چاہئے؟ جواب نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ نفع یہاں مقصود نہیں بلکہ مقصود مال مضاربت ہے۔ بہر حال تابع کو یہاں متبوع کے درجہ میں رکھ کر شفعہ جاری نہیں کیا گیا اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں تابع یعنی بیع کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ متبوع یعنی نکاح کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔
From this discussion, when it became known that here marriage (nikah) is the original and sale is subordinate, then when there is no preemption (shuf'ah) in marriage i.e. the original, then preemption will not be established in the sale which is subordinate. Then the second principle is that preemption is established in a financial exchange where financial consideration is intended. Here marriage is intended, not financial exchange as became clear from the mentioned discussion. Can you provide an example of this? Yes, the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) gave one thousand rupees to a mudarib for trade. He traded and gained one thousand profit. Then the mudarib bought a house for two thousand. Then he sold it. The owner of capital had the right of preemption; he claimed preemption in that house. Will the owner of capital get preemption? The answer was: No, it will not be given. Why? Because the owner of capital is in the position of principal (muwakkil) and the mudarib is agent (wakil), and the sale of the agent is the sale of the principal. So this becomes as if the owner himself sold and himself claimed preemption. Question: Regarding the one thousand profit in that, why not consider the mudarib as agent and the owner as principal, and for half the house which is the share of profit, the owner should get preemption? Answer: It will not be given because profit is not intended here; rather the capital of mudaraba is intended. Nevertheless, the subordinate is not given the status of the original in establishing preemption; similarly, in the mentioned issue, the subordinate i.e. sale is not considered; rather the original i.e. marriage is considered.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that preemption (shuf'ah) is not established in a sale that is subordinate to a non-financial contract such as marriage (nikah). The author first reiterates the earlier conclusion: since nikah itself does not give rise to shuf'ah, the sale that accompanies a marriage contract (like dower) also does not carry shuf'ah. He then states the general principle: shuf'ah is only established in a purely financial exchange (mubadala mali) where financial consideration is the primary object. Nikah is not a financial exchange. He then provides an illustrative example from mudaraba: when a mudarib uses capital to buy and then sell a house, the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) cannot claim shuf'ah against that sale because the sale is treated as if done by the owner himself through his agent. Even for the portion of the house corresponding to profit, shuf'ah is not allowed because the primary object is the mudaraba capital, not the profit. This confirms the rule that shuf'ah does not arise in sales that are subordinate to non-financial contracts.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Right of preemption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property that has been sold to a third party under certain conditions.
مضارب (mudarib): The agent in a mudaraba partnership who invests the capital and manages the trade.
رب المال (rabb al-mal): The owner of capital in a mudaraba contract, who provides the funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mudaraba example, why does the owner of capital (rabb al-mal) not get shuf'ah when the mudarib sells the house?
A) Because the mudarib is not a proper agent
B) Because the sale is considered as the owner's own sale
C) Because the house was bought with profit only
D) Because shuf'ah is only for neighbors

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah requires a purely financial exchange; a sale that is subordinate to nikah or an agent's sale in mudaraba does not give rise to shuf'ah.

Ruling on Donkey Meat, Milk, and Camel Urine (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Statements from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on donkey meat/milk and camel urine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on donkey meat and milk in the Hanafi school, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on camel urine, and apply the ruling to medicinal scenarios.

Core Idea
Donkey meat is makruh tahrimi; camel urine is disputed: Abu Hanifa says haram, Sahibayn permit it (at least for medicine).

This passage presents two related but distinct rulings: the first on donkey meat and milk, agreed upon as makruh tahrimi by all three founding Hanafi imams; the second on camel urine, which reveals a significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Understanding the proofs and practical consequences of each position is essential for a mufti navigating medical fatawa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
Find the ruling on donkey meat and milk. Note that all three imams agree it is makruh (tahrimi). The milk takes the ruling of the meat.
This is an uncontested point within the school.
2
Identify the disputed substance
Locate the discussion of camel urine. Note that Abu Hanifa rules it makruh (or haram, according to the commentary), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree.
The disagreement is on camel urine, not on donkey milk.
3
Trace each imam's proof (dalil)
Abu Hanifa argues from the original impurity of urine and restricts the Urainiyyin hadith to that specific incident. Abu Yusuf uses the same hadith to permit for medicine. Muhammad invokes the general principle that Allah does not place cure in what He has forbidden.
Each dalil is naqli, but they are interpreted differently.
4
Understand the ta'wil of Abu Yusuf's statement
The text explains that Abu Yusuf's 'no harm' is interpreted as limited to medicinal use (li al-tadawi), not absolute permissibility.
This ta'wil harmonizes Abu Yusuf's view with the general caution.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, camel urine is forbidden even for medicine; according to Abu Yusuf, it is allowed for medicine; according to Muhammad, it is allowed for any purpose. The mufta bihi in later practice often adopts the Sahibayn's view for necessity.
The same substance can yield three different fatwas depending on which view is operative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گدھی کا گوشت اور دودھ اور اونٹ کا پیشاب مکروہ ہے
فال ابو حنيفة يكره لحوم الاتن والبانها وابوال الابل وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد لا باس بابوال الابل وتاويل قول ابى يوسف انه لا باس بها للتداوى وقد بينا هذه الجملة فيما تقدم في الصلوة والذبائح فلا نعيدها واللبن متولد من اللحم فاخذ حكمه.
ترجمه. فرمایا ابوحنیفہ نے گدھیوں کے گوشت اور ان کے دودھ مکروہ ہیں اور اونٹوں کے پیشاب اور ابو یوسف اور محمد نے فرمایا کہ اونٹوں کے پیشابوں میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور ابو یوسف کے قول کی تاویل یہ ہے کہ ان میں دواء کے لئے ( استعمال میں ) کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور ہم نے ان تمام کو ماقبل میں کتاب الصلوۃ اور ذبائح میں بیان کر دیا ہے پس ہم ان کا اعادہ نہیں کریں گے اور خودوہ گوشت سے پیدا ہوتا ہے تو لے لے گا۔ دودھ گوشت کے حکم کو ۔ تشریح گدھا اور گدھی کا گوشت مکروہ ہے یعنی مکروہ تحریمی اور گدھی کا دودھ بھی مکروہ ہے اور ایسے ہی اونٹ کا پیشاب بھی مکروہ ہے اور کراہت کی وجہ سے اس میں ائمہ کا اختلاف ہے۔
امام صاحب نے اس کو حرام قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ پیشاب میں اصل حرمت ہے اور ر با اصحاب عربینہ کے واقعہ سے استدلال تو وہ درست نہیں کیوں کہ وہاں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کو ان کی شفاء کا علم وحی کے ذریعہ ہو گیا تھا تو غیر کے زر میں حکم حرمت برقرار ر ہیگا اور اسی حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہوئے امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ دواء کے لئے حلال ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مطلقاً حلال ہے کیوں کہ اگر یہ حلال نہ ہوتا تو اس سے دواء و علاج بھی درست نہ ہوتا۔ کیوں کہ حدیث میں ہے ما وضع شفاء كم فيما حرم علیکم مصنف خود اس مسئلہ کو کتاب الصلواۃ اور کتاب الذبائح میں بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
سوال .... وہاں دودھ کا تو ذکر نہیں آیا ؟
The meat and milk of female donkeys and camel urine are makruh. Abu Hanifa said: The meat of female donkeys and their milk are makruh, and camel urine. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no harm in camel urine. The interpretation of Abu Yusuf's statement is that there is no harm in it for medicinal use. We have already explained this topic in the books of Prayer and Slaughter, so we will not repeat it. Milk is generated from meat, so it takes the ruling of meat. Explanation: The meat of male and female donkeys is makruh, i.e., makruh tahrimi, and the milk of female donkeys is also makruh, and similarly camel urine is makruh. There is disagreement among the imams regarding its dislike. Imam Abu Hanifa declared it haram because the original ruling of urine is prohibition, and the argument from the incident of the Urainiyyin is not valid because there the Prophet (peace be upon him) knew of their cure through revelation, so the ruling of prohibition remains for others. Using the same hadith, Imam Abu Yusuf said it is permissible for medicinal purposes, and Imam Muhammad considered it absolutely permissible because if it were not permissible, then medicinal treatment with it would not be valid, as the hadith says: 'He did not place your cure in what He has forbidden for you.' The author himself has explained this issue in the Book of Prayer and the Book of Slaughter. Question: There, milk was not mentioned?
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents a specific fiqh ruling on the meat of female donkeys, their milk, and camel urine, along with the intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states: 'Abu Hanifa said: The meat of female donkeys and their milk, and camel urine are makruh. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is no harm in camel urine.' The commentary explains that Abu Yusuf's permission is restricted to medicinal use, while Imam Muhammad permits it absolutely. The ruling on donkey meat and milk is that they are makruh tahrimi according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn do not differ on that point. The dispute centers on camel urine. Abu Hanifa considers it haram because urine is fundamentally impure and prohibited, and the hadith of the Urainiyyin (where the Prophet allowed camel urine for treatment) does not establish general permissibility because the Prophet had special knowledge through revelation. Abu Yusuf uses the same hadith to permit it for medicine. Imam Muhammad argues from the general principle that healing is not placed in forbidden things, so if camel urine were forbidden, it could not be used as medicine; since it is used in medicine, it must be inherently permissible. The author notes that the full discussion is in earlier chapters (Salah and Dhabaih). A student's question about milk not being mentioned there is left open.

Key Terms
لحوم الأتن (luhum al-utun): The meat of female donkeys; ruled as makruh (makruh tahrimi) by Abu Hanifa.
ألبان الأتن (alban al-utun): The milk of female donkeys; takes the ruling of the meat, so it is also makruh.
أبوال الإبل (abwal al-ibil): Camel urine; disputed among Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh/haram, Abu Yusuf permits for medicine, Muhammad permits absolutely.
التداوي (al-tadawi): Medical treatment; Abu Yusuf permits camel urine specifically for this purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on camel urine according to Imam Abu Yusuf?
A) It is absolutely haram.
B) It is makruh tahrimi.
C) It is permissible for medicinal purposes.
D) It is absolutely halal.

Key Takeaway
Donkey meat and milk are makruh tahrimi; camel urine is disputed among Hanafi imams, with later practice often permitting it for medicine.

Attending a Feast with Singing or Play
Ruling on attending a walima or feast where sinful entertainment is present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attending a feast with sinful entertainment, explain the proof (hadith), and apply the principle of weighing obligations.

Core Idea
Attending a feast with singing is permissible because the duty to accept the invitation outweighs the presence of sin.

Imagine you are invited to a wedding feast (walima) and upon arrival you find music and singing that are considered sinful. Should you leave immediately, or stay and eat? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling that balances the obligation to accept invitations with the prohibition of participating in sin. This lesson explores the evidence and reasoning behind that ruling, guiding you through the legal analysis of such situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
Recognize that the act in question is accepting a general invitation to a meal (or specifically a walima). The default ruling for accepting is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) based on the hadith.
The text says 'sunnah' but some Hanafis consider it wajib for a walima.
2
Locate and Understand the Proof
The proof cited is the hadith: 'Whoever does not answer the invitation has disobeyed Aba al-Qasim' (i.e., the Prophet). This shows the seriousness of refusing an invitation.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) according to Hanafis.
3
Analyze the Exception: Presence of Sin
When sinful entertainment is present, the default ruling to accept might conflict with the duty to avoid sin. The Hanafi position is that the obligation to accept is not nullified; one should still attend and eat, and try to stop the sin if possible.
This is supported by analogy to funeral prayer: obligatory even if wailing (sin) is present.
4
Apply the Principle: Weighing Obligations
The ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle of weighing conflicting obligations: the stronger duty (accepting the invitation, especially for walima) takes precedence over the lesser harm (presence of sin). One should intend to disapprove and, if able, prevent the sin.
If unable to prevent, patience is recommended; do not miss the virtue of accepting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن دعى الى وليمة أو طعام فوجد ثمه لعباً أوغناء فلا بأس بان يقعد وياكل قال ابو حنيفة ابتليت بهذا مرة فصبرت وهذا لان اجابة الدعوة سنة قال عليه السلام من لم يجب الدعوة فقد عصى أبا القاسم فلا يتركها لما اقترنت به من البدعة من غيره كصلوة الجنازة واجبة الاقامة وان حضرتها نياحة فان قدر على المنع منعهم وان لم يقدر يصبر ترجمہ محمد نے (جامع صغیر میں ) فرمایا اور جس کو ولیمہ یا کسی اور کھانے کی دعوت دی گئی پس اس نے وہاں لہو ولعب یا گانا بجانا پایا تو کوئی حرج نہیں کہ بیٹھ جائے اور کھائے ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا میں اس میں ایک مرتبہ پھنس گیا تو میں نے صبر کیا اور یہ اس لئے کہ دعوت کو قبول کرنا سنت ہے فرمایا نبی علیہ السلام نے جس نے دعوت قبول نہیں کی تو اس نے ابا القاسم ( محمد رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نافرمانی کی تو دعوت کو نہ چھوڑے اس وجہ سے کہ اس کے ساتھ اس کے غیر کی جانب سے بدعت ملی ہوئی ہے جیسے نماز جنازہ قائم کرنا واجب ہے اگر چہ اس میں رونا پیٹنا ہو پس اگر وہ روکنے پر قادر ہے تو اس کو روکے اور اگر قادر نہ ہو تو صبر کرے۔ تشریح ولیمہ یا کسی اور دعوت میں مدعو کیا گیا اور وہاں جا کر دیکھا کہ گانا بجانا ہو رہا ہے یا خلاف شرع لہو لعب ہے تو فرمایا کہ بیٹھ کر کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ حضرت امام صاحب بھی ایک دفعہ اس میں پھنسے تھے تو انہوں نے فرمایا کہ میں نے صبر کیا یعنی بیٹھ کر
He said: And whoever is invited to a walima (wedding feast) or food and finds there play or singing, there is no harm in his sitting and eating. Abu Hanifa said: I was afflicted with this once and I exercised patience. This is because accepting the invitation is sunnah. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever does not answer the invitation has disobeyed Aba al-Qasim.' So he should not leave it due to the innovation that has accompanied it from another, like the funeral prayer: its establishment is obligatory even if wailing is present. If he is able to prevent them, he should prevent them; if he is not able, he should be patient. Commentary: [...]
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on attending a wedding feast (walima) or any meal invitation where there is sinful entertainment such as singing or play. The source is Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir. The ruling is that it is permissible to sit and eat because the obligation to accept the invitation (sunnah mu'akkadah according to the Hanafis, but the hadith indicates it is necessary) takes precedence over the disliked presence of entertainment. Abu Hanifa himself once found himself in such a situation and chose to remain patiently. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever does not respond to the invitation has disobeyed Aba al-Qasim,' showing the gravity of refusing. The commentary analogizes to the funeral prayer: if one attends a funeral where wailing (a sin) occurs, it is still obligatory to perform the prayer, and one should try to stop the sin if possible; otherwise, one should bear it. Similarly, in a feast, the primary duty is to accept the invitation, and one should try to forbid the evil, but if unable, one should remain and eat rather than miss the virtue of accepting. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle of weighing obligations and avoiding harm.

Key Terms
وليمة (walima): The feast given after marriage; a specific type of invitation.
دعوة (da'wah): General invitation to a meal; accepting is sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi school say about attending a walima where there is singing and play?
A) It is haram to attend; one must leave immediately
B) It is permissible to sit and eat, and one should try to stop the wrongdoing if possible
C) One may attend but must not eat anything
D) One should only attend if there is no singing; otherwise it is makruh

Key Takeaway
When obligations conflict, the stronger duty (accepting the invitation) takes precedence over the lesser evil (presence of sin), and one should try to correct the sin if possible.

Walima Timing and Accepting Invitations
Rulings on walima timing and invitation acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of walima and the ruling on accepting invitations.

Core Idea
Walima is after consummation; accepting invitations is sunnah, with some authorities saying wajib.

This lesson covers two related aspects of social conduct: the proper time for the wedding feast (walima) and the obligation to accept invitations. These rulings come from later Hanafi authorities as cited in the tanbihat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Define walima: a wedding feast hosted by the groom. The first admonition asks about its timing.
2
Determine the time
The text cites Hafiz Ibn Hajar that the walima is at the time of consummation or after. This is the preferred Hanafi view.
Some earlier opinions suggested before, but the cited evidence indicates after.
3
Ruling on accepting invitations
The second admonition states that if there is no impediment, one should accept the invitation. Some say it is sunnah, but Fatawa Tatarkhaniya says wajib.
The difference affects whether missing without excuse is sinful.
4
Consult the authorities
Note that the sources are Fath al-Bari (for walima) and al-Shami and Fatawa Tatarkhaniya (for invitations). These are later Hanafi references.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ - ولیمہ کا وقت کیا ہے؟ حافظ ابن حجر نے فتح الباری ص ۲۳۰ ج ۱ پر اقوال مختلفہ پیش کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے فدل على انها عند الدخول او بعده - تنبیه - ولیمہ کی دعوت ہو یا اور اگر کوئی مانع نہ ہو تو دعوت قبول کرے بعض نے قبول کرنے کو سنت اور فتاوی تا تارخانیہ میں واجب کہا ہے۔ والبسط فی الشامی ص ۲۱۱ ج ۵ تنبیہ - اگر دستر خوان پر غیبت ہورہی ہو تو اس کا حکم بھی ملائی جیسا ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۲۱ ج ۵ تنبیہ - جولوگ منکر فعل میں مبتلا ہیں ان پر نکیر کرنے کے لئے اجازت کے بغیر دخول جائز ہے، شامی ص ۲۲۲ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه - ۶ اپنے نفس کی ہلاکت کو دور کرنے کے لئے کھانا فرض ہے اور ایسے ہی ستر عورت اور بدن کو گرمی اور سردی سے بچانا اور پیٹ بھر کھانا مباح ہے اور اگر اس سے بھی زیادہ کھائے جس میں فساد معدہ کا ظن ہو تو یہ حرام ہے مگر مہمان کی رعایت میں یا زندہ پر قوت کے لئے اتنا کھانا حلال ہے۔ تنبیہ کے ننگے سر کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے ، شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیہ - ۸ کھانے سے پہلے جوانوں کے ہاتھ ڈھلانے سے ابتداء کی جائے گی اور کھانے سے فراغت کے بعد بوڑھوں سے ہاتھ ڈھلانے کی ابتداء کی جائے گی۔ شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه 9 جس نے مخمصہ کی حالت میں مردار سے احتراز کیا یا روزہ رکھا اور مر گیا تو وہ گنہگار ہوگا البتہ اگر بیماری میں دوا نہیں ں اور مکی تو گندگا نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ دوا سے صحت کا یقین نہیں ہے بلکہ بغیر علاج کے بھی صحیح ہوسکتا ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۰۵ ج ۲۔ تنبیه ۱۰ اپنے نفس کو اتنا بھوکا رکھنا کہ عبادات کی ادائیگی میں خلل واقع نہ ہو حلال ہے، حوالہ بالا۔ تنبیه بهترین پیشہ جہاد پھر تجارت، پھر زراعت پھر ضباعت ، مجمع الا نبرص ۵۰۸ ج ۲ پیشہ
Admonition - What is the time of walima? Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari, vol. 1, p. 230, after presenting different opinions: 'So it indicates that it is at the time of consummation or after.' Admonition - Whether it is a walima invitation or another, if there is no impediment, one should accept the invitation. Some said it is sunnah, and in Fatawa Tatarkhaniya it is said to be wajib. And the detail is in al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 211. Admonition - If there is backbiting on the table, its ruling is like that of musical entertainment. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 221. Admonition - Entering without permission for the purpose of forbidding people engaged in forbidden acts is permissible. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 222. Admonition 6 - Eating to ward off destruction of oneself is fard, and similarly covering the private parts and protecting the body from heat and cold. Eating to fill the stomach is mubah. If one eats more than that such that there is a presumption of stomach disorder, it is haram, except for the sake of hospitality or to gain strength for worship, in which case it is halal. Admonition - There is no harm in eating with an uncovered head. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 216. Admonition 8 - Before eating, one should begin with washing the hands of the young, and after finishing, begin with washing the hands of the old. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 216. Admonition 9 - Whoever in a state of hunger refrains from carrion or fasts and dies, he will be sinful. However, if he does not take medicine in sickness and dies, he will not be sinful because certainty of health from medicine is not assured; rather, he may recover without treatment. Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 505. Admonition 10 - Keeping oneself so hungry that it does not cause disruption in performing acts of worship is halal. Same reference. Admonition - The best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship? Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 508. Profession.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This set of admonitions (tanbihat) provides several independent rulings. First, it specifies that the walima (wedding feast) should be after consummation. Second, it notes that accepting any invitation without impediment is sunnah, but some Hanafi fatwa collections say it is wajib. Third, if backbiting occurs at the table, the ruling is the same as for musical entertainment (i.e., one should leave). Fourth, entering a place without permission to enjoin good and forbid evil is allowed. Fifth, eating to preserve life is fard, but overeating that harms is haram, except for hospitality or strength for worship. Sixth, eating bare-headed is permissible. Seventh, the order of washing hands: start with the young before eating and with the old after eating. Eighth, if one refrains from eating carrion in dire hunger and dies, he sins; but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful because recovery is not guaranteed. Ninth, moderate hunger that does not affect worship is permissible. Tenth, the best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. These are all concise rulings from later Hanafi works like al-Shami and Majma' al-Anhar.

Key Terms
ولی (muja): A wedding feast hosted by the groom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Before the wedding
B) At the time of consummation or after
C) Anytime within the first week
D) Only after children are born

Key Takeaway
Walima is after consummation; accepting invitations is sunnah muakkadah.

Backbiting at the Table and Entering Without Permission for Nahi Anil Munkar
Rulings on backbiting and entering for nahi anil munkar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaving a gathering where backbiting occurs, and the permissibility of entering without permission to forbid evil.

Core Idea
If backbiting occurs at a meal, the ruling is like musical entertainment (leave); entering without permission to forbid evil is allowed.

These two admonitions address situations where a Muslim is exposed to sin: attending a gathering where backbiting takes place, and needing to intervene in wrongdoing. Hanafi fiqh provides clear guidance to uphold the duty of forbidding evil while maintaining propriety.

Guided Path
1
First situation: backbiting at the table
The text says the ruling is 'like musical entertainment' (ملائی). This refers to the prohibition of staying where sin is committed; one should leave or advise against it.
The ruling is from al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 221.
2
Second situation: entering without permission
If people are engaged in forbidden acts, one may enter their premises without explicit permission to stop them, because the obligation to enjoin good overrides privacy rights.
This is permissible only if it is safe and effective.
3
Recognize the common principle
Both rulings prioritize avoiding sin and fulfilling the duty of hisbah over minor proprieties like remaining seated or seeking permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیہ - ولیمہ کا وقت کیا ہے؟ حافظ ابن حجر نے فتح الباری ص ۲۳۰ ج ۱ پر اقوال مختلفہ پیش کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے فدل على انها عند الدخول او بعده - تنبیه - ولیمہ کی دعوت ہو یا اور اگر کوئی مانع نہ ہو تو دعوت قبول کرے بعض نے قبول کرنے کو سنت اور فتاوی تا تارخانیہ میں واجب کہا ہے۔ والبسط فی الشامی ص ۲۱۱ ج ۵ تنبیہ - اگر دستر خوان پر غیبت ہورہی ہو تو اس کا حکم بھی ملائی جیسا ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۲۱ ج ۵ تنبیہ - جولوگ منکر فعل میں مبتلا ہیں ان پر نکیر کرنے کے لئے اجازت کے بغیر دخول جائز ہے، شامی ص ۲۲۲ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه - ۶ اپنے نفس کی ہلاکت کو دور کرنے کے لئے کھانا فرض ہے اور ایسے ہی ستر عورت اور بدن کو گرمی اور سردی سے بچانا اور پیٹ بھر کھانا مباح ہے اور اگر اس سے بھی زیادہ کھائے جس میں فساد معدہ کا ظن ہو تو یہ حرام ہے مگر مہمان کی رعایت میں یا زندہ پر قوت کے لئے اتنا کھانا حلال ہے۔ تنبیہ کے ننگے سر کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے ، شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیہ - ۸ کھانے سے پہلے جوانوں کے ہاتھ ڈھلانے سے ابتداء کی جائے گی اور کھانے سے فراغت کے بعد بوڑھوں سے ہاتھ ڈھلانے کی ابتداء کی جائے گی۔ شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه 9 جس نے مخمصہ کی حالت میں مردار سے احتراز کیا یا روزہ رکھا اور مر گیا تو وہ گنہگار ہوگا البتہ اگر بیماری میں دوا نہیں ں اور مکی تو گندگا نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ دوا سے صحت کا یقین نہیں ہے بلکہ بغیر علاج کے بھی صحیح ہوسکتا ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۰۵ ج ۲۔ تنبیه ۱۰ اپنے نفس کو اتنا بھوکا رکھنا کہ عبادات کی ادائیگی میں خلل واقع نہ ہو حلال ہے، حوالہ بالا۔ تنبیه بهترین پیشہ جہاد پھر تجارت، پھر زراعت پھر ضباعت ، مجمع الا نبرص ۵۰۸ ج ۲ پیشہ
Admonition - What is the time of walima? Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari, vol. 1, p. 230, after presenting different opinions: 'So it indicates that it is at the time of consummation or after.' Admonition - Whether it is a walima invitation or another, if there is no impediment, one should accept the invitation. Some said it is sunnah, and in Fatawa Tatarkhaniya it is said to be wajib. And the detail is in al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 211. Admonition - If there is backbiting on the table, its ruling is like that of musical entertainment. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 221. Admonition - Entering without permission for the purpose of forbidding people engaged in forbidden acts is permissible. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 222. Admonition 6 - Eating to ward off destruction of oneself is fard, and similarly covering the private parts and protecting the body from heat and cold. Eating to fill the stomach is mubah. If one eats more than that such that there is a presumption of stomach disorder, it is haram, except for the sake of hospitality or to gain strength for worship, in which case it is halal. Admonition - There is no harm in eating with an uncovered head. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 216. Admonition 8 - Before eating, one should begin with washing the hands of the young, and after finishing, begin with washing the hands of the old. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 216. Admonition 9 - Whoever in a state of hunger refrains from carrion or fasts and dies, he will be sinful. However, if he does not take medicine in sickness and dies, he will not be sinful because certainty of health from medicine is not assured; rather, he may recover without treatment. Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 505. Admonition 10 - Keeping oneself so hungry that it does not cause disruption in performing acts of worship is halal. Same reference. Admonition - The best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship? Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 508. Profession.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This set of admonitions (tanbihat) provides several independent rulings. First, it specifies that the walima (wedding feast) should be after consummation. Second, it notes that accepting any invitation without impediment is sunnah, but some Hanafi fatwa collections say it is wajib. Third, if backbiting occurs at the table, the ruling is the same as for musical entertainment (i.e., one should leave). Fourth, entering a place without permission to enjoin good and forbid evil is allowed. Fifth, eating to preserve life is fard, but overeating that harms is haram, except for hospitality or strength for worship. Sixth, eating bare-headed is permissible. Seventh, the order of washing hands: start with the young before eating and with the old after eating. Eighth, if one refrains from eating carrion in dire hunger and dies, he sins; but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful because recovery is not guaranteed. Ninth, moderate hunger that does not affect worship is permissible. Tenth, the best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. These are all concise rulings from later Hanafi works like al-Shami and Majma' al-Anhar.

Key Terms
ملائی (mulai): Musical entertainment; in context, a reference to gatherings where sinful music is played, which one must leave or avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on entering without permission to forbid people engaged in forbidden acts?
A) It is haram
B) It is permissible
C) It is makruh
D) It is fard

Key Takeaway
Leave backbiting gatherings; enter without permission to stop sin when safe.

Rules of Eating: Preservation, Overeating, and Etiquette
Rulings on eating: obligation, prohibition, and etiquette.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi rulings on eating: when it is fard, mubah, haram, and the proper etiquette including hand washing and bareheadedness.

Core Idea
Eating to preserve life is fard; overeating with harm is haram; etiquette includes washing hands of young first before eating and old after.

This lesson compiles several admonitions related to eating: the obligation to eat when in danger of death, the prohibition of harmful overeating, and the sunan of eating, including covering the head and hand washing order. These rulings reflect the balance between preserving life, avoiding harm, and following prophetic etiquette.

Guided Path
1
Identify the levels of eating
The text grades eating: fard (to ward off death), mubah (to fill stomach without harm), haram (if overeating leads to stomach disorder), and halal with intention (for hospitality or worship).
The permissions change based on intention and harm.
2
Etiquette: bareheadedness and hand washing
Eating bareheaded is permissible (no harm). Hand washing: before eating, start with the young; after eating, start with the old.
These are adab (etiquette) not obligatory.
3
Moderate hunger for worship
Keeping oneself hungry to the extent that worship is not disrupted is halal.
Excessive hunger that hinders worship is not recommended.

Life Preservation: Carrion in Extreme Hunger vs Medicine
Ruling on avoiding carrion in hunger vs medicine in illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that avoiding carrion in dire hunger resulting in death is sinful, while avoiding medicine in illness is not sinful.

Core Idea
Refusing carrion in hunger causing death is sinful because survival is certain; refusing medicine is not sinful because recovery is uncertain.

This admonition draws a sharp distinction between two situations of avoiding a means of preservation: food in extreme hunger and medicine in sickness. The difference hinges on certainty: while eating carrion when starving guarantees survival, taking medicine does not guarantee recovery. Hence, the rulings differ.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario of makhmasah
Makhmasah is severe hunger threatening life. In such a state, it is obligatory (fard) to eat even haram food like carrion to survive.
This overrides the prohibition of carrion because necessity permits the forbidden.
2
Sin of refraining from food
If a person refrains from eating carrion or fasts (even voluntarily) and dies, he is sinful because he failed to preserve his life when the means were certain.
The sin is for omitting a fard act.
3
Medicine scenario
If a person is sick and does not take medicine, and dies, he is not sinful because medicine does not guarantee recovery; one may recover without it.
Certainty of benefit is lacking.
4
Identify the legal principle
The key is certainty (yaqeen): when preservation of life is certain, it becomes fard; when uncertain, it remains optional.

Source Text

Best Professions: Jihad, Trade, Agriculture, Craftsmanship
Ranking of professions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ranking of professions as jihad, trade, agriculture, and craftsmanship.

Core Idea
The best profession is jihad, then trade, agriculture, then craftsmanship.

This final admonition provides a hierarchy of occupations from a religious perspective. It reflects the value placed on defending the faith, providing for oneself and others through honest work, and the lesser rank of manual trades.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ranking
The text lists: best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship (ضباعت, likely a typo for صناعت).
This ranking is based on the text of Majma' al-Anhar.
2
Understand the reasons
Jihad is highest because it involves sacrifice for the faith. Trade and agriculture are praised because they benefit the community. Craftsmanship is last among these.
All professions are permissible, but some are superior in reward.
3
Apply the hierarchy
When choosing a career, Muslims should prefer these fields in this order, but individual circumstances may vary.
This is not a strict obligation but a guidance.

تنبیہ - ولیمہ کا وقت کیا ہے؟ حافظ ابن حجر نے فتح الباری ص ۲۳۰ ج ۱ پر اقوال مختلفہ پیش کرنے کے بعد فرمایا ہے فدل على انها عند الدخول او بعده - تنبیه - ولیمہ کی دعوت ہو یا اور اگر کوئی مانع نہ ہو تو دعوت قبول کرے بعض نے قبول کرنے کو سنت اور فتاوی تا تارخانیہ میں واجب کہا ہے۔ والبسط فی الشامی ص ۲۱۱ ج ۵ تنبیہ - اگر دستر خوان پر غیبت ہورہی ہو تو اس کا حکم بھی ملائی جیسا ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۲۱ ج ۵ تنبیہ - جولوگ منکر فعل میں مبتلا ہیں ان پر نکیر کرنے کے لئے اجازت کے بغیر دخول جائز ہے، شامی ص ۲۲۲ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه - ۶ اپنے نفس کی ہلاکت کو دور کرنے کے لئے کھانا فرض ہے اور ایسے ہی ستر عورت اور بدن کو گرمی اور سردی سے بچانا اور پیٹ بھر کھانا مباح ہے اور اگر اس سے بھی زیادہ کھائے جس میں فساد معدہ کا ظن ہو تو یہ حرام ہے مگر مہمان کی رعایت میں یا زندہ پر قوت کے لئے اتنا کھانا حلال ہے۔ تنبیہ کے ننگے سر کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے ، شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیہ - ۸ کھانے سے پہلے جوانوں کے ہاتھ ڈھلانے سے ابتداء کی جائے گی اور کھانے سے فراغت کے بعد بوڑھوں سے ہاتھ ڈھلانے کی ابتداء کی جائے گی۔ شامی ص ۲۱۶ ج ۵ ۔ تنبیه 9 جس نے مخمصہ کی حالت میں مردار سے احتراز کیا یا روزہ رکھا اور مر گیا تو وہ گنہگار ہوگا البتہ اگر بیماری میں دوا نہیں ں اور مکی تو گندگا نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ دوا سے صحت کا یقین نہیں ہے بلکہ بغیر علاج کے بھی صحیح ہوسکتا ہے۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۰۵ ج ۲۔ تنبیه ۱۰ اپنے نفس کو اتنا بھوکا رکھنا کہ عبادات کی ادائیگی میں خلل واقع نہ ہو حلال ہے، حوالہ بالا۔ تنبیه بهترین پیشہ جہاد پھر تجارت، پھر زراعت پھر ضباعت ، مجمع الا نبرص ۵۰۸ ج ۲ پیشہ
Admonition - What is the time of walima? Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari, vol. 1, p. 230, after presenting different opinions: 'So it indicates that it is at the time of consummation or after.' Admonition - Whether it is a walima invitation or another, if there is no impediment, one should accept the invitation. Some said it is sunnah, and in Fatawa Tatarkhaniya it is said to be wajib. And the detail is in al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 211. Admonition - If there is backbiting on the table, its ruling is like that of musical entertainment. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 221. Admonition - Entering without permission for the purpose of forbidding people engaged in forbidden acts is permissible. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 222. Admonition 6 - Eating to ward off destruction of oneself is fard, and similarly covering the private parts and protecting the body from heat and cold. Eating to fill the stomach is mubah. If one eats more than that such that there is a presumption of stomach disorder, it is haram, except for the sake of hospitality or to gain strength for worship, in which case it is halal. Admonition - There is no harm in eating with an uncovered head. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 216. Admonition 8 - Before eating, one should begin with washing the hands of the young, and after finishing, begin with washing the hands of the old. Al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 216. Admonition 9 - Whoever in a state of hunger refrains from carrion or fasts and dies, he will be sinful. However, if he does not take medicine in sickness and dies, he will not be sinful because certainty of health from medicine is not assured; rather, he may recover without treatment. Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 505. Admonition 10 - Keeping oneself so hungry that it does not cause disruption in performing acts of worship is halal. Same reference. Admonition - The best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship? Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 508. Profession.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This set of admonitions (tanbihat) provides several independent rulings. First, it specifies that the walima (wedding feast) should be after consummation. Second, it notes that accepting any invitation without impediment is sunnah, but some Hanafi fatwa collections say it is wajib. Third, if backbiting occurs at the table, the ruling is the same as for musical entertainment (i.e., one should leave). Fourth, entering a place without permission to enjoin good and forbid evil is allowed. Fifth, eating to preserve life is fard, but overeating that harms is haram, except for hospitality or strength for worship. Sixth, eating bare-headed is permissible. Seventh, the order of washing hands: start with the young before eating and with the old after eating. Eighth, if one refrains from eating carrion in dire hunger and dies, he sins; but not taking medicine in illness is not sinful because recovery is not guaranteed. Ninth, moderate hunger that does not affect worship is permissible. Tenth, the best profession is jihad, then trade, then agriculture, then craftsmanship. These are all concise rulings from later Hanafi works like al-Shami and Majma' al-Anhar.

Key Terms
ضباعت (daba'at): Craftsmanship; likely a scribal variant for صناعت (craft) or صباعت (dyeing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Trade
B) Agriculture
C) Jihad
D) Craftsmanship

Key Takeaway
Jihad is the best profession, followed by trade, agriculture, and craftsmanship.

Looking at Non-Mahram Woman's Face When Fear of Desire Exists
Stating the prohibition of looking with desire and the exception for need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at a non-mahram woman's face when desire is feared, and apply the criterion of 'la ya'man' to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Looking at a non-mahram woman's face is haram if desire is present or feared, even if doubt, and only permitted for genuine need.

This lesson examines a key exception to the general permissibility of looking at a non-mahram woman's face. The Hanafi school teaches that while the face itself is not awrah, looking becomes prohibited when desire is present or reasonably feared. We will explore the textual proof and the precise scope of the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is looking at a non-mahram woman's face. State the base ruling: permissible when safe from desire, but prohibited (haram) when desire is present or feared.
The ruling changes based on subjective state.
2
Understand the condition of 'amn'
Recognize that 'amn min al-shahwah' (safety from desire) is the key condition for permissibility. If one does not feel secure (la ya'man), the ruling becomes prohibition.
The author expands 'la ya'man' to include doubt, certainty, and predominant opinion.
3
Learn the exception of 'hajah'
Identify that a legitimate need (hajah) such as giving testimony, intending marriage, or buying a female slave can make looking permissible even when desire is feared. The need must be genuine and not excessive.
Needs are limited to shari'ah-recognized purposes.
4
Apply the subjective standard
Apply the principle that even doubt about one's desire triggers the prohibition. The standard is subjective: if a man knows, thinks, or doubts that looking will arouse desire, he must refrain unless there is a need.
This reflects Hanafi caution in guarding against prohibited acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان كان لا يامن الشهوة لا ينظر الى وجهها الا لحاجة لقوله عليه السلام من نظر الى محاسن امراة اجنبية عن شهوة صب في عينيه الأنك يوم القيمة فان خاف الشهوة لم ينظر من غير حاجة تحرزاً عن المحرم وقـولـه لا يـامـن يـدل على انه لا يباح اذا شك في الاشتهاء كما اذا علم او كان اكبر رأيه ذلک
He said: 'If he does not feel secure from desire, he should not look at her face except for a need' because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever looks at the beauty of a non-mahram woman with desire, on the Day of Judgment molten lead will be poured into his eyes.' So if he fears desire, he should not look without a need, guarding against the prohibited. And his saying 'does not feel secure' indicates that it is not permissible when he doubts concerning desiring, just as when he knows or his predominant opinion is that.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on looking at a non-mahram woman's face. The earlier statement (that it is permissible) is conditioned on being safe from desire (amn al-shahwah). If a man fears desire or knows he will desire, looking becomes prohibited (haram) without a genuine need. The hadith (though considered weak by some scholars like al-Zayla'i and Ibn Hajar) warns of a severe punishment for lustful looks. Imam al-Quduri's phrase 'does not feel secure' (la ya'man) includes cases of doubt, certainty, or predominant opinion. Thus, even uncertainty about one's inclination makes it impermissible to look unnecessarily.

Key Terms
لا يامن (la ya'man): Not feeling secure from desire; includes cases of certainty, predominant opinion, or doubt about arousing desire.
حاجة (hajah): A legitimate need such as testimony, intention to marry, or buying a female slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only when there is certainty of desire.
B) When one doubts, has predominant opinion, or knows that desire will arise.
C) Only if one looks for pleasure.
D) It is never prohibited if her face is uncovered.

Key Takeaway
Looking at a non-mahram woman's face is haram when desire is present or feared, and the threshold includes uncertainty; only a genuine need lifts the prohibition.

Touching a Non-Mahram Woman: Prohibition and Exception
Prohibiting touching even without desire due to lack of necessity and a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching a non-mahram woman's face and hands, distinguish between young and old women, and apply the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Touching a young non-mahram woman is haram even without desire; for an old woman it is permissible if safe from fitnah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical social interaction: physical contact with a non-mahram woman. While looking may be permissible under certain conditions due to necessity, the scholars rule more strictly on touching. The author provides a hadith as evidence and then makes an important distinction between young and old women, based on the presence or absence of fear of fitnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Touching the face or hand of a non-mahram woman. The ruling is haram for a young woman.
The act is explicit: 'yamsu wajhaha wa la kaffaha'.
2
Understand the rationale
Why is touching prohibited even if safe from desire? Because the prohibition (hurmah) stands and there is no necessity or general affliction (balwa) as in looking.
The text says 'liqiyam al-muhrim wa'n'idam al-darurah wa al-balwa'.
3
Examine the proof
What is the textual evidence? The hadith threatens punishment for touching a woman not lawfully related.
The hadith is cited: 'Man massa kaffa al-mar'ati laysa minha bisebil...'
4
Identify the exception
When does the ruling change? For an old woman not desired, touching is permissible due to absence of fitnah.
The condition is 'idha kanat 'ajuzan la tushtaha'.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
How do other schools view this? Hanbali: no exception. Shafi'i: some allow with barrier.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يحل له ان يمس وجهها ولا كفها وان كان يامن الشهوة لقيام المحرم وانعدام الضرورة والبلوى بخلاف النظر لان فيه بلوى والمحرم قوله عليه السلام من مس كف المرأة ليس منها بسبيل وضع على كفه جمر يوم القيمة وهذا اذا كانت شابة تشتهى ما اذا كانت عجوزا لا تشتهي فلا بأس بمصافحتها ومس يدها لانعدام خوف الفتنة
And it is not permissible for him to touch her face nor her palm even if he is safe from desire, because the prohibition stands and there is no necessity nor general affliction, unlike looking because there is general affliction in it. And the prohibiting (text) is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever touches the palm of a woman with whom he has no lawful relationship, a hot coal will be placed on his palm on the Day of Judgment.' And this applies when she is a young woman who is desired; as for when she is an old woman not desired, there is no harm in shaking her hand and touching her hand due to the absence of fear of fitnah.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage differentiates the ruling on touching from looking. Even if a man is safe from desire, touching a non-mahram woman's face or hands is prohibited. The reason: there is no overwhelming necessity ('adam al-darurah) and no general affliction (balwa) like in the case of looking. Additionally, a specific hadith threatens punishment for touching a woman without a lawful relationship. However, this prohibition is qualified: it applies to young women who are typically desired (tushtaha). For an old woman (ajuz) who is not desired, shaking her hand or touching her hand is permissible because there is no fear of fitnah. This exception is supported by the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr (may Allah be pleased with them) who shook hands with old women and employed an old woman nurse.

Key Terms
بلوى (balwa): General affliction or widespread occurrence; here refers to the common necessity of looking at women in daily transactions.
فتنة (fitnah): Temptation or trial; specifically the fear of falling into sin due to desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on touching a non-mahram woman's hand if she is old (ajuz)?
A) Haram under all circumstances.
B) Permissible because there is no fear of fitnah.
C) Permissible only if she is a mahram.
D) Makruh but not haram.

Key Takeaway
Touching a young non-mahram woman is haram even without desire; for an old woman, it is permissible when safe from fitnah.

Ruling on Looking at a Female Slave One Intends to Buy
Ruling on looking at a slave woman with fear of desire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at a slave woman for purchase and identify the condition that changes permissibility to prohibition.

Core Idea
Looking at a female slave for purchase is only permissible when safe from desire; any fear of desire makes it haram.

The Hanafi school permits looking at a female slave one intends to buy, but this permission is conditional on safety from desire (aman min al-shahwa). If there is fear of desire, even doubt, looking becomes haram. This passage from al-Hidayah explains the ruling, citing a weak hadith but relying on stronger evidence and the principle of avoiding haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
The act is looking at a female slave with the intention of purchase. The default ruling is permissibility, but it is conditional.
This is a specific exception to the general prohibition of looking at non-mahram.
2
Examine the Hadith Evidence
A hadith 'man nazara...' is mentioned but declared gharib by Zaylai and not found by Ibn Hajar. Other authentic hadith support the prohibition with desire.
The weak hadith does not stand alone; the ruling is reinforced by other texts and principles.
3
Understand the Condition: Safety from Desire
Imam Quduri states that if one is not safe from desire (ma'mun), one should not look. This means any fear, even doubt, triggers prohibition.
The condition is psychological: certainty, strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann), or mere doubt of desire all make looking haram.
4
Apply the Ruling to Scenarios
Apply: if no desire is felt and no fear arises, looking is permissible. If there is any fear, it is haram to avoid the prohibited.
This is a precautionary principle (sadd al-dhara'i) to prevent sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہو، یا باندی ہے جس کو خریدنے کا ارادہ ہو اس سلسلہ میں یہ حدیث وارد ہے من نظر الخ لیکن علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ غریب ہے اور ابن حجر نے کہا ہے لم اجدہ ،البتہ دیگر احادیث صحاح وعید میں وارد ہیں، اگر دیکھنے میں شہوت کا خوف ہوتب بھی بغیر حاجت کے نہیں دیکھے گا تا کہ حرام سے احتراز ہو۔ امام قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ جب شہوت سے مامون نہ ہو تو نہیں دیکھے گا اس سے یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ اگر اس کو شہوت ہونے کا شک ہو تب بھی دیکھنا جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ یقین اور گمان غالب کی صورت میں جائز نہیں ہے۔
He, or a slave woman whom he intends to buy. In this regard, this hadith is narrated: 'man nazara...' etc. But Allama Zaylai says that it is gharib, and Ibn Hajar said: 'I did not find it.' However, other authentic hadith are narrated in books of promise and threat. If there is fear of desire in looking, then even without necessity, he should not look, in order to avoid the haram. Imam Quduri said: When he is not safe from desire, he should not look. From this it is understood that if he has doubt of desire, then looking is not permissible, just as it is not permissible in case of certainty or strong presumption.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the situation of looking at a female slave one intends to purchase. The hadith mentioned is considered weak by Zaylai and not found by Ibn Hajar, but other authentic hadith exist on the topic. The ruling is that if there is any fear of desire, looking is prohibited even without necessity. Imam Quduri's statement further clarifies that even doubt of desire triggers prohibition, similar to certainty or dominant presumption. This is to avoid the haram. The passage does not discuss the case of looking at a free woman, which is generally prohibited, but here the permission for looking at a slave is conditional on safety from desire.

Key Terms
شہوت (shahwa): Sexual desire or lust, which triggers prohibition of looking.
مامون (ma'mun): Being safe from the influence of desire, i.e., confident one will not fall into haram.
غریب (gharib): A hadith classification meaning rare or weak in transmission at some level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible
B) Impermissible
C) Recommended
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of looking at a slave for purchase is conditional on being safe from desire; any fear or doubt makes it haram.
