Ruling on Looking at a Woman One Intends to Marry
Explanation of permissibility to look at a prospective spouse to foster compatibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at a prospective bride, identify the primary textual evidence, and explain the rationale based on intention.

Core Idea
Looking at a prospective wife is permissible and recommended to foster marital harmony.

This lesson examines the permissibility of a man looking at a woman he intends to marry. The Hanafi school, relying on a direct prophetic command, permits this even when desire is known, as long as the intention is to follow the Sunnah and assess compatibility. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between the act's permissibility and the intention behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling on looking at a prospective bride according to the Hanafi school. Is it prohibited, permissible, or recommended? Cite the basis.
The ruling is mubah (permissible) and actually mustahab (recommended) due to the hadith.
2
Identify the primary evidence (dalil)
Locate the hadith cited in the passage. Record the exact wording and its source.
The hadith: 'Look at her, for it is more likely to create harmony between you two.' (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah)
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
Explain why looking is permitted despite the general prohibition of looking at non-mahram women. Focus on the intention and the goal of harmony.
The purpose is to follow the Sunnah and prevent future discord, not to fulfill desire.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may restrict looking to face and hands. Contrast the Hanafi reasoning.
Hanafis give weight to the specific hadith over the general prohibition, allowing more extensive looking if needed for compatibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ارادان يتزوج امرأة فلا باس بان ينظر اليها وان علم ان يشتهيها لقوله عليه السلام فيه ابصرها فانه احرى ان يودم بينكما ولان مقصوده اقامة السنة لا قضاء الشهوة
ترجمہ اور جس نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کا ارادہ کیا تو اس کی جانب دیکھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اگر چہ اس کو اس بات کا یقین ہو کہ اس کو اس کی شہوت ہوگی نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے اس کے بارے میں کہ اس کو دیکھ لو پس یہ زیادہ لائق ہے کہ تم دونوں کے درمیان موافقت پیدا کر دی جائے اور اس لئے کہ اس کا مقصود سنت کو اداء کرنا ہے نہ کہ شہوت کو پورا کرنا۔
تشریح جس عورت سے نکاح کرنا چاہتا ہے اس کو دیکھنا جائز ہے اگر چہ ثبوت کا خطرہ ہو کیوں کہ اس کا مقصود قضاء شہوت نہیں ہے بلکہ سنت پر عمل کرنا ہے کیوں ایسے موقع پر بارگاہ رسالت سے دیکھنے کا حکم صادر ہوا ہے ارشاد ہے ابصر هافانه احرى ان يؤدم بينكما (رواہ الترمذی والنسائی وابن ماجہ ) کیوں کہ دیکھنے سے یہ معلوم ہو جائے گا کہ دونوں میں موافقت ہے یا نہیں ورنہ بسا اوقات میاں بیوی کے درمیان موافقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بات کہیں سے کہیں پہونچ جاتی ہے۔ ادم اور ایدام کے معنی اصلاح اور توفیق کے ہیں۔
And whoever intends to marry a woman, there is no harm in looking at her, even if he knows that he will desire her, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning her: "Look at her, for it is more likely to create harmony between you two." And because his purpose is to follow the Sunnah, not to fulfill desire. Translation: And whoever intends to marry a woman, there is no harm in looking at her, even if he is certain that he will have desire for her, because of the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning her: "Look at her, for it is more likely to create harmony between you two." And because his purpose is to follow the Sunnah, not to fulfill desire. Explanation: Looking at the woman one intends to marry is permissible, even if there is a risk of desire, because his purpose is not to fulfill desire but to act upon the Sunnah. On such an occasion, the command to look came from the court of prophethood. The guidance is: "Look at her, for it is more likely to create harmony between you two" (narrated by Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah). Because by looking, it becomes known whether there is compatibility between the two; otherwise, sometimes due to lack of harmony between husband and wife, matters escalate. The words 'adm' and 'idām' mean reconciliation and harmony.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a man who intends to marry a woman: it is permissible to look at her, even if he knows he will feel desire. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) commanded a man to look at a prospective bride, saying it is more likely to create harmony. The key distinction is the intention: the purpose is to follow the Sunnah and determine compatibility, not to fulfill desire. This is a special permission granted for the sake of marriage, overriding the general prohibition of looking at non-mahram women. The Hanafi school emphasizes that this looking is recommended (mustahab) because it helps avoid future discord.

Key Terms
نکاح (nikah): Marriage contract; looking is permitted for the purpose of marriage.
سنت (sunnah): The prophetic practice; here, looking is part of following the Sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ).
ادم/ایدام (adm/idam): Reconciliation and harmony between spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a man looking at a woman he intends to marry?
A) Prohibited because she is non-mahram.
B) Permissible only if he looks without desire.
C) Permissible and recommended, even if he knows he will desire her.
D) Permissible only once before the marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility to look at a prospective spouse is based on prophetic guidance to create harmony, and the ruling is governed by intention, not by the mere presence of desire.

Permissibility of Looking at Wife or Slave-Girl's Private Parts
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a man looking at his wife's private parts and cite the hadith evidence for its permissibility.

Core Idea
A man may look at his wife's private parts; the Prophet explicitly excepted spouses from the command to lower the gaze.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling that balances permission with modesty. The primary proof is a direct hadith that exempts one's wife and slave-girl from the general command to lower the gaze. We'll explore the text, the exception, and the qiyas that reinforces permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a man looking at the private parts (farj) of his wife or his amah (female slave that is halal for him). The ruling is permissibility (mubah) in absolute terms, with or without desire.
The text uses the term 'مته' which is likely a typo for 'أمته' (his slave-girl).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith: 'غض بصرك الا عن امتك وامرأتك' (Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife) is cited as the root (al-asl).
This is a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase is 'الا عن' (except from), which creates an exception. The general command to lower the gaze (ghadd al-basar) is universal, but this exception removes the wife and slave-girl from that prohibition.
In Hanafi usul, a command with an exception is clear in its meaning (dalala qati'iyya) even if the transmission (thubut) of this hadith is zanni.
4
Consider the qiyas (analogy)
The text adds: since intercourse and touching (masis wa ghishyan) are permissible, looking is even more so (awla). This is a qiyas aulawi (analogy with superior applicability).
This reinforces the permissibility by reasoning that if the more intimate act is mubah, the lesser act of looking must also be mubah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرد کیلئے اپنی باندی اور بیوی کی شرم گاہ کو دیکھنے کا حکم
قال وينظر الرجل من مته التي تحل له وزوجته الى فرجها وهذا اطلاق في النظر الى سائر بدنها عن شهوة وغير شهوة والاصل فيه قوله عليه السلام غض بصرك الا عن امتك وامرأتك ولان ما فوق ذلك من المسيس والغشيان مباح فالنظر اولى الا ان الاولى ان لا ينظر كل واحد منهما الى عورة صاحبه لقوله عليه السلام اذا اتى احدكم اهله فليستتر ما استطاع ولا يتجردان تجرد العير ولان ذلك يورث النسيان لورود الاثر وكان ابن عمر رضى الله عنهما يقول الأولى ان ينظر ليكون ابلغ في تحصيل معنى اللذة
Ruling for a man looking at his slave-girl that is permissible for him and his wife: He may look at her private parts. And this is absolute regarding looking at all parts of her body with desire or without desire. The basis for this is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife.' And because what is beyond that, i.e., touching and intercourse, is permissible, so looking is even more so. Except that it is better that neither of them look at the private parts of the other, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'When one of you goes to his wife, let him cover himself as much as he can, and let them not strip like the stripping of a donkey.' And because that causes forgetfulness, as reported in the tradition. And Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) used to say: It is better to look, so as to better achieve the meaning of pleasure.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith regarding a man looking at the private parts of his wife and his slave-girl (umm walad or simply his female slave). It states it is permissible absolutely, with or without desire. The proof is the hadith: 'Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife' (a hadith from the Prophet). Additionally, since intercourse itself is permissible, looking is even more so (qiyas with inferior degree). However, the text notes that it is better (al-awla) not to look at each other's private parts, based on another hadith that advises covering and not stripping like donkeys, and because it may cause forgetfulness. Then it mentions that Ibn Umar held the view that looking is better to achieve greater pleasure. This shows two opinions within the Hanafi school: one prefers looking (to enhance pleasure), the other prefers not looking (out of modesty). The text presents both but does not explicitly choose one, though the structure 'الا ان الاولى ان لا ينظر' suggests that the preferred (afdal) is to avoid looking.

Key Terms
فرج (farj): Private parts, genitals
امت (amah): Female slave that is halal for the master
غض بصر (ghadd al-basar): Lowering the gaze, commanded in Quran

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Consensus of the Companions
B) The Prophet's hadith: 'Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife'
C) Analogy with looking at one's own bodily parts
D) The verse of the Quran on modesty

Key Takeaway
A man may look at his wife's private parts, but it is recommended (mustahabb) to observe modesty and avoid looking when possible.

The Preferable Practice: Modesty Over Looking
Expansion on preferred practice from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers it better for spouses not to look at each other's private parts, and contrast this with Ibn Umar's view.

Core Idea
Although looking is permissible, modesty (haya') and the Prophetic sunna recommend covering and avoiding the sight of private parts.

After establishing permissibility, the passage introduces a higher standard: it is better (al-awla) not to look. This is based on another Prophetic instruction and a reported effect of forgetfulness. We'll examine this preference and the dissenting opinion of Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the better practice (al-awla)
The text states 'الا ان الاولى ان لا ينظر' (except that it is better not to look). This is a recommendation of preference, not a prohibition.
The word 'الاولى' indicates a higher level of religious merit, similar to mustahabb.
2
Analyse the second hadith
The hadith: 'اذا اتى احدكم اهله فليستتر ما استطاع ولا يتجردان تجرد العير' (When one of you goes to his wife, let him cover as much as he can, and let them not strip like the stripping of a donkey). This counsels covering and avoiding complete nudity.
The comparison to a donkey's stripping implies a lack of modesty.
3
Consider the additional reason (forgetfulness)
The text mentions that looking causes forgetfulness (yurith al-nisyan) as reported in tradition. This is a psychological or spiritual effect that discourages looking.
The exact tradition is not cited, but it adds weight to the preference.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Ibn Umar
Ibn Umar held that looking is better because it enhances pleasure (al-ladhdha). The passage records this as a counterview but does not endorse it.
This shows that even within the early generation, there was a range of opinion on the best practice.

Ruling on Viewing a Spouse's Private Parts in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with proof on permissibility of viewing spouse's private parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a man looking at his wife's or slave-girl's private parts, identify the primary proof (hadith exception), and distinguish between permissibility and the preferred practice.

Core Idea
Looking at spouse's private parts is permissible but better to avoid; the hadith exception allows it.

This lesson examines the classical Hanafi position on a man viewing his wife's or slave-girl's private parts. The passage from al-Hidayah presents the ruling as permissible (mubah) with supporting proofs, but also introduces a preference (awla) for modesty. Understanding this distinction is important to avoid common misconceptions that it is prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling
The act is a man looking at the private parts of his wife or permissible slave-girl. The default ruling in the matn is permissibility (mubah), not obligation or prohibition.
Note that the ruling applies regardless of desire.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'غض بصرك الا عن امتك وامرأتك' (Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife). This is a specific exception to the general command to lower the gaze.
The hadith is the basis for the exception.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogical) reasoning
Since touching and intercourse are explicitly permitted, looking is a fortiori (اولیٰ) permissible. The reasoning is that if the greater act is allowed, the lesser act (looking) is even more appropriate.
Qiyas strengthens the permissibility.
4
Distinguish between the ruling and the awla (preferred practice)
The text then presents a preference (awla): it is better not to look, based on another hadith about covering during intimacy and the claim that looking may cause forgetfulness. However, this does not change the ruling of permissibility.
The awla is a recommendation, not a requirement.
5
Note the critical evaluation of supporting hadiths
The commentator notes that the hadith about forgetfulness is weak, and the narration from Ibn Umar suggesting looking is better is not reliably attributed. The operative ruling remains permissibility.
Authenticity affects the weight of the preferred practice.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وينظر الرجل من مته التي تحل له وزوجته الى فرجها وهذا اطلاق في النظر الى سائر بدنها عن شهوة وغير شهوة والاصل فيه قوله عليه السلام غض بصرك الا عن امتك وامرأتك ولان ما فوق ذلك من المسيس والغشيان مباح فالنظر اولى الا ان الاولى ان لا ينظر كل واحد منهما الى عورة صاحبه لقوله عليه السلام اذا اتى احدكم اهله فليستتر ما استطاع ولا يتجردان تجرد العير ولان ذلك يورث النسيان لورود الاثر وكان ابن عمر رضى الله عنهما يقول الأولى ان ينظر ليكون ابلغ في تحصيل معنى اللذة
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرد دیکھے اپنی باندی سے جو اس کے لئے حلال ہے اور اپنی بیوی سے اس کی فرج کی جانب اور یہ اجازت ہے اس کے پورے بدن دیکھنے کی شہوت سے اور بغیر شہوت کے اور اصل میں نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ اپنی نظر کو رو کونگر اپنی باندی سے اور اپنی بیوی سے اور اس لئے کہ وہ چیز جو اس سے بڑھ کر ہے یعنی چھونا اور جماع مباح ہے تو دیکھنا بدرجہ اولی مگر اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کی عورت کی جانب نہ دیکھے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ جب تم میں سے کوئی اپنی بیوی کے پاس آئے تو جہاں تک وہ سکے ستر کریں اور اونٹ کی طرح دونوں ننگے نہ ہو جائیں اور اس لئے کہ یہ ( شرمگاہ کی جانب دیکھنا ) نسیان کو پیدا کرتا ہے اور اثر کے وارد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ ادنیٰ یہ ہے کہ دیکھے تا کہ ہو جائے یہ زیادہ بلیغ لذت کے معنی کی تحصیل میں ۔ تشریح مرد اپنی بیوی اور وہ باندی کا جو اس کے لئے حلال ہے سارا بدن دیکھ سکتا ہے خواہ شہوت ہو یا نہ ہو کیوں کہ جب چھونا اور ولی کرنا جائز ہے تو پھر دیکھنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہو گا مگر بہر حال عورت نہ دیکھا اولیٰ ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو یہاں مذکور ہے مگر ابن عمر سے عورت کے دیکھنے کی فضیلت منقول ہے کیوں کہ یہ زیادہ لذت کا باعث ہے۔

تنبیه - ۳ مورث نسیان کا اثر بقول علامہ زیلعی غریب ہے اور مورث علی کی احادیث ضعیف ہیں۔ تنبیہ - ۴ ابن عمر کے اثر کے بارے میں علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں قلت غریب جدا ، اور علامہ عینی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ابن عمر سے بالکل ثابت نہیں ہے نہ مسند صحیح ہے اور نہ سند ضعیف ہے۔
He said: A man looks at his slave-girl who is permissible for him and his wife at her private part. This includes looking at her entire body with or without desire. Its basis is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife.' And because what is above that, of touching and intercourse, is permissible, so looking is even more appropriate. However, it is better that neither of them looks at the other's private part due to his saying: 'When one of you goes to his wife, let him cover as much as he can, and let them not become naked like the donkey.' And because that causes forgetfulness, as the effect has been reported. And Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to say: It is better to look, because it is more effective in achieving the pleasure. Commentary: A man may see his wife and his permissible slave-girl's entire body, with or without desire, because when touching and intercourse are permissible, looking is even more so. However, it is better not to look at the private part due to the mentioned hadith. But Ibn Umar narrates the virtue of looking for greater pleasure. Notifications: The first hadith is not found with these exact words, but the meaning is found in multiple hadiths. The second hadith is found in Ibn Majah and Tabarani. The effect causing forgetfulness is rare according to Allama Zayla'i, and hadiths about forgetfulness are weak. Regarding Ibn Umar's narration, Allama Zayla'i says it is extremely rare, and Allama Ayni says it is not established from Ibn Umar at all.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage rules on a man looking at his wife's or slave-girl's private parts. The matn asserts it is permissible (mubah) to look at her private parts, and this extends to the entire body regardless of desire. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Lower your gaze except from your slave-girl and your wife.' This is a specific exception to the general command to lower the gaze. Additionally, since physical intimacy (touching, intercourse) is permitted, looking is a fortiori permissible. However, the text then presents a preference (awla) that spouses should not look at each other's private parts, based on another hadith instructing modesty during intimacy and warning against complete nakedness like donkeys. A narrated effect states it may cause forgetfulness. Yet a contrary narration from Ibn Umar suggests looking is better for enhancing pleasure. The commentary clarifies that these are preferences, not prohibitions. The commentator includes critical notes on the authenticity of the hadiths: the first hadith is not verbatim but its meaning is authentic; the second hadith is found in Ibn Majah and Tabarani; the effect about forgetfulness is weak; and Ibn Umar's statement is not reliably attributed. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) remains permissibility, with the better practice being to avoid looking at the private parts.

Key Terms
شرم گاہ (sharmgah): Private parts (genitals).
اولیٰ (awla): Better/preferable, not obligatory.
نسیان (nisyan): Forgetfulness, claimed as a negative effect of looking at private parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Permissible, but better to avoid
C) Only permissible with intent of desire
D) Makruh tahrimi

Key Takeaway
Looking at spouse's private parts is permissible in Hanafi fiqh, but avoiding it is preferred based on weaker evidence.

Ruling on Viewing Mahram Women: Permissible and Prohibited Parts
Ruling on permissible viewing of mahram women with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which body parts a man may see of his mahram female relatives and identify the Quranic proof that supports the ruling.

Core Idea
A man may see face, head, chest, shins, and arms of mahram women; back, belly, and thigh remain awrah.

The boundaries of awrah extend even to mahram relatives. This lesson clarifies exactly what a man may or may not look at of his female mahrams, based on the Quranic permission to reveal 'zina' (adornment) to specified relatives. Understanding this ruling prevents both excessive restriction and undue laxity in family interactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a man looking at his female mahram relatives. The ruling is that it is permissible to see certain parts and prohibited to see others. List the permitted parts: face, head, chest, shins, upper arms. List the prohibited parts: back, belly, thigh.
The matn (primary text) enumerates exactly five permissible and three prohibited areas.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 24:31: 'And let them not reveal their adornment except to their husbands...' (ولا يبدين زينتهن الا لبعولتهن). The verse permits showing 'zina' (adornment) to mahrams.
The word 'zina' is interpreted in Hanafi fiqh to mean 'places of adornment'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi school understands 'zina' as the places where adornment is worn (e.g., face for earrings, neck for necklace, arms for bangles). Therefore, the verse permits showing those body parts to mahrams. The prohibition on back, belly, and thigh follows because they are not places of adornment.
This is a linguistic interpretation (tafsir) based on customary usage.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) define 'zina' more broadly to include the adornment itself, leading to differences in what may be revealed. However, the Hanafi position is based on the literal meaning of 'zina' as it appears in the Quran.
The practical difference mainly affects what parts are considered awrah between mahrams.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is supported by the zahir (apparent meaning) of the verse and is relied upon for fatwa. The supplementary parts (forearm, ear, neck, foot) are included as they are also places of adornment.
This ruling is from the principal (zahir al-riwayah) works of the school.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وينظر الرجل من ذوات محارمه الى الوجه والرأس والصدر والساقين والعضدين ولا ينظر الى ظهرها وبطنها وفخذها والاصل فيه قوله تعالى ولا يبدين زينتهن الا لبعولتهن الآية والمرادو الله اعلم مواضع الزينة وهى ما ذكرنا فى الكتاب ويدخل في ذلك الساعد والاذن والعنق والقدم لان ذلك مواضع الزينة بخلاف الظهر والبطن والفخذلانها ليست مواضع الزينة
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرد دیکھے اپنی محارم سے چہرے اور سر اور سینہ اور پنڈلی اور بازؤں کی جانب اور نہ دیکھے اس کی پیٹھ اور پیٹ اور اس کی ران کی جانب اور اصل اس میں فرمان باری تعالیٰ ہے اور ظاہر نہ کریں اپنی زینت کو مگر اپنے شوہروں اور السخ اور مراد والله اعلم مواضع زینت ہیں اور وہ وہ ہیں جن کو ہم کتاب میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور اس میں کلائی اور کان اور گلا اور قدم داخل ہیں اس لئے کہ یہ سب زینت کی جگہ میں بخلاف پیٹھ اور پیٹ اور ان کے اس لئے کہ یہ مواضع زینت نہیں ہیں۔
تشریح جو عورتیں مرد کی ذی رحم محرم میں ان کا چہرہ سر سینہ، پنڈلی، بازود یکھ سکتا ہے اور پیٹ اور پیٹھ ان نہیں دیکھ سکتا۔ کیونکہ اس آیت مذکورہ میں اپنے محارم کے لئے زینت کو ظاہر کرنے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے اور زینت سے مراد مواضع زینت ہیں
He said: A man looks at his mahram females at the face, head, chest, shins, and upper arms; and he does not look at her back, belly, and thigh. Its basis is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And let them not reveal their adornment except to their husbands...' and the meaning, Allah knows best, is the places of adornment, which are what we have mentioned in the book. This includes the forearm, ear, neck, and foot because they are places of adornment, unlike the back, belly, and thigh because they are not places of adornment. Commentary: Women who are mahram by kinship: a man may see their face, head, chest, shins, and arms; he may not see the belly and back. Because in the mentioned verse, permission is given to reveal adornment to mahrams, and 'adornment' refers to the places of adornment.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage details what a man may and may not see of his female mahram (permanently unmarriageable relatives). The matn specifies five permissible parts: face, head, chest, shins, and upper arms. The prohibited parts are the back, belly, and thigh. The proof is Quran 24:31: '...and let them not reveal their adornment except to their husbands...' The verse allows revealing 'zina' (adornment) to specified relatives, and the Hanafi interpretation takes 'zina' to mean the places where adornment is worn—such as the face (earrings), neck (necklace), arms (bangles), feet (anklets), etc. Thus, these areas are permissible to see. The back, belly, and thigh are not places for adornment, so they remain awrah. The commentary adds that the forearm, ear, neck, and foot are also included in the permissible category. The ruling is based on a clear Quranic text, making it a strong precedent. Note that this is for mahram relatives; for non-mahram, more restrictions apply.

Key Terms
محارم (mahārim): Female relatives whom a man cannot marry due to blood, marriage, or fosterage.
زینت (zīnat): Adornment; here referring to the places where jewelry is worn (face, neck, arms, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following may a man NOT see of his mahram?
A) Face and head
B) Chest and arms
C) Belly and back
D) Shins and feet

Key Takeaway
A man may only see the face, head, chest, shins, and arms of his mahram relative; all other parts, especially the back, belly, and thigh, remain awrah.

Looking at One's Spouse: Permissibility and Better Practice
Statement of permissibility and recommendation for covering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a man looking at his wife's body and explain the proof (dalil) and the recommendation (afdal) to cover.

Core Idea
A man may see his wife's entire body, but covering during intimacy is better.

The Hanafi school affirms that a husband can look at his wife's entire body, with or without desire. This permissibility is based on a Prophetic command to restrain the gaze and a clear analogy (qiyas) from the permissibility of touching and intercourse. However, the text also presents a stronger practice: covering one's private parts during intimacy, supported by another hadith. In this lesson, we will unpack the ruling, its proofs, and the nuances of recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement by al-Quduri: the man may look at his wife and slave woman, even at the private part, with or without desire. Note that the hukm level is mubah (permissible).
2
Examine the Primary Proof (Dalil Naqli)
The text cites the Prophet's command: 'Restrain your gaze from your slave woman and your wife.' Understand how the command implies permission for the opposite—since restriction is commanded, the absence of restriction indicates permissibility.
The exact wording is not found in major hadith collections, but the meaning is corroborated.
3
Trace the Rational Proof (Qiyas)
The text argues: since touching and intercourse are permissible, seeing—which is a lesser act—is even more so (bi darajat al-ula). This is a clear qiyas jaliy.
4
Identify the Recommendation and Its Proof
Despite the permissibility, the better practice (afdal) is to cover during intimacy, based on another hadith: 'When one of you comes to his wife, let him cover...' Also note the report from Ibn 'Umar that looking enhances pleasure, though its authenticity is weak.
The recommendation is a nuance: mubah yet better to cover.
5
Evaluate the Authenticity Notes
Read the four notes (tanbihat): the first hadith is not verbatim but its meaning is authentic; the second hadith is in Ibn Majah and Tabarani; the hadith about forgetfulness are weak; the report from Ibn 'Umar is unreliable. This teaches that legal rulings can rely on hadith of zanni thubut when supported by qiyas.
The commentator has done the critical work of validating the proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرد دیکھے اپنی باندی سے جو اس کے لئے حلال ہے اور اپنی بیوی سے اس کی فرج کی جانب اور یہ اجازت ہے اس کے پورے بدن دیکھنے کی شہوت سے اور بغیر شہوت کے اور اصل میں نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ اپنی نظر کو رو کونگر اپنی باندی سے اور اپنی بیوی سے اور اس لئے کہ وہ چیز جو اس سے بڑھ کر ہے یعنی چھونا اور جماع مباح ہے تو دیکھنا بدرجہ اولی مگر اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کی عورت کی جانب نہ دیکھے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ جب تم میں سے کوئی اپنی بیوی کے پاس آئے تو جہاں تک وہ سکے ستر کریں اور اونٹ کی طرح دونوں ننگے نہ ہو جائیں اور اس لئے کہ یہ ( شرمگاہ کی جانب دیکھنا ) نسیان کو پیدا کرتا ہے اور اثر کے وارد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ ادنیٰ یہ ہے کہ دیکھے تا کہ ہو جائے یہ زیادہ بلیغ لذت کے معنی کی تحصیل میں ۔ تشریح مرد اپنی بیوی اور وہ باندی کا جو اس کے لئے حلال ہے سارا بدن دیکھ سکتا ہے خواہ شہوت ہو یا نہ ہو کیوں کہ جب چھونا اور ولی کرنا جائز ہے تو پھر دیکھنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہو گا مگر بہر حال عورت نہ دیکھا اولیٰ ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو یہاں مذکور ہے مگر ابن عمر سے عورت کے دیکھنے کی فضیلت منقول ہے کیوں کہ یہ زیادہ لذت کا باعث ہے۔
تنبیہ - ا پہلی حدیث ان الفاظ کے ساتھ نہیں ملی البتہ یہ مفہوم دوسرے الفاظ کے ساتھ متعدد احادیث میں موجود ہے۔ تنبیه - دوسری حدیث ابن ماجہ اور طبرانیہ میں موجود ہے۔
تنبیه - ۳ مورث نسیان کا اثر بقول علامہ زیلعی غریب ہے اور مورث علی کی احادیث ضعیف ہیں۔ تنبیہ - ۴ ابن عمر کے اثر کے بارے میں علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں قلت غریب جدا ، اور علامہ عینی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ابن عمر سے بالکل ثابت نہیں ہے نہ مسند صحیح ہے اور نہ سند ضعیف ہے۔
The Book of Disliked Matters. Quduri said: And a man looks at his slave woman who is lawful for him and at his wife, towards her private part, and this is permission to see her entire body, with desire and without desire. The original proof is the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Restrain your gaze from your slave woman and your wife.' And because that which is greater than it, i.e., touching and intercourse, is permissible, so seeing is even more so. But it is better that each of them does not look at the private part of the other, due to the Prophet's saying: 'When one of you comes to his wife, let him cover as much as he can, and let them not both be naked like a camel.' And because this (looking at the private part) causes forgetfulness, and due to the effect narrated. And Ibn 'Umar says: 'The least is that he should look so that it becomes more effective in obtaining extreme pleasure.' Explanation: A man can see the entire body of his wife and his slave woman who is lawful for him, whether with desire or not, because when touching and intimacy are permissible, then seeing is even more so. But in any case, it is better that the wife does not look, due to the hadith mentioned here. However, from Ibn 'Umar, the virtue of the woman looking is transmitted, because it leads to greater pleasure. Note 1: The first hadith is not found with these exact words, but its meaning is present in multiple hadith with other words. Note 2: The second hadith is found in Ibn Majah and Tabarani. Note 3: The effect of causing forgetfulness, according to 'Allama Zayla'i, is strange, and the hadith that cause it are weak. Note 4: Regarding the effect of Ibn 'Umar, 'Allama Zayla'i said: 'I say it is extremely strange,' and 'Allama 'Ayni said: 'This is not established at all from Ibn 'Umar, neither with a sound chain nor with a weak chain.'
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding a man's gaze towards his wife and his slave woman. The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that a man may look at the entire body of his wife and his lawful slave woman, both with and without sexual desire. The proof is a hadith commanding restraint of gaze, and a rational argument (qiyas): since touching and intercourse are permissible, seeing is even more so. However, the text also notes a better practice: it is preferable for each spouse to avoid looking at the other's private parts during intimacy, based on another hadith. The passage also includes a report from Ibn 'Umar suggesting that looking enhances pleasure. Four notes follow regarding the authenticity of the hadith: the first hadith is not verbatim but its meaning is authentic; the second hadith is from Ibn Majah and Tabarani; the hadith about forgetfulness are weak; and Ibn 'Umar's report is not reliably attributed to him.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Gazing, looking with the eyes.
شہوت (shahwa): Sexual desire.
باندی (bandi): Slave woman owned by a man, whom he may have intercourse with.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is prohibited (haram).
B) It is permissible (mubah) but better to cover.
C) It is obligatory (wajib).
D) It is only allowed without desire.

Key Takeaway
A man may see his wife's entire body with or without desire, but covering during intimacy is the better practice.

Nikah — Marriage

8 min
Ruling on a Man Looking at His Mahram Women
Ruling with proof from Quran and rational argument on mahram looking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible and prohibited body parts of mahram women, identify the Quranic proof (24:31), and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on zina creating mahramiyyah.

Core Idea
A man may see mahram women's customary places of adornment but not the back, belly, or thigh.

This lesson clarifies which parts of a mahram woman a man may see according to the Hanafi school. The ruling is based on Quran 24:31, which permits displaying adornment to mahrams, interpreted as the places where jewelry is worn. A rational argument (istihsan) based on daily interaction and hardship supports the ruling. The lesson also addresses a key dispute: whether zina (fornication) creates mahramiyyah, with the preferred view being that it does, allowing the man to look at the woman as a mahram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage to list the body parts a man may see (face, head, chest, shins, arms) and those he may not (back, belly, thigh). Note that forearm, ear, neck, and foot are also included as places of adornment.
The list is based on customary adornment places.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is Quran 24:31, which allows displaying zeenah (adornment) to mahrams. The Hanafi interpretation takes zeenah as the places of adornment, hence the listed body parts.
The proof is qati al-thubut (Quran) but zanni al-dalalah (interpretation).
3
Understand the rational proof (istihsan)
The text gives a rational reason: mahrams enter each other's homes without formality, and women are often in work clothes. Prohibiting all looking would cause hardship (haraj). Also, desire decreases due to perpetual prohibition.
This is an example of istihsan based on necessity.
4
Define mahram and examine the zina dispute
A mahram is one with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (by lineage, fosterage, or affinity). Some early Hanafi scholars argued that affinity through zina does not permit looking because it is a punishment. The asahh (most correct) view holds that it does, as the woman becomes perpetually forbidden, and the same hardship rationale applies.
The tarjih is given by later authorities like al-Haskafi and Ibn 'Abidin.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a man visiting his sister (mahram by blood). He may see her head and chest but should avoid her belly and thigh. If he had zina with a woman, according to the asahh view, she becomes mahram and the same permissibility applies.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.

ولان البعض يدخل على البعض من غير استيذان واحتشام والمرأة فى بيتها فى ثياب مهنتها عادة فلو حرم النظر " الى هذه المواضع ادى الى الحرج وكذا الرغبة تقل للحرمة الموبدة فقل ما تشتهي بخلاف ما ورائها لانها لا تنكشف عادة والمحرم من لا تجوز المناكحة بينه وبينها على التابيد بنسب كان او بسبب كالرضاع والمصاهرة لوجود المعنين فيه وسواء كانت المصاهرة بنكاح اوسفاح في الاصح لما بينا
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ بعض بعض پر بغیر اجازت اور بغیر شرم و حیا کے داخل ہوتا ہے اور عورت عادۃ اپنے گھر میں اپنے کام کاج کے کپڑوں میں رہتی ہے تو اگر ان جگہوں کی جانب دیکھنا حرام کر دیا جائے تو یہ مفضى الى الحرج ہوگا اور ایسے ہی حرمت موبد کی وجہ سے رغبت کم ہوتی ہے تو شہوت کم ہوتی ہے بخلاف ان اعضاء کے جو ان کے علاوہ ہیں (پیٹ، پیٹھ، ران ) اس لئے کہ یہ عادہ نہیں کھلتے اور محرم وہ ہے کہ اس کے اور اس عورت کے درمیان ہمیشہ مناکحت جائز نہ ہو نسب کی وجہ سے ہو یا سبب کی وجہ سے جیسے دودھ پینے اور مصاہرت کی وجہ سے دونوں معنی (ضرورت اور قلت رغبت) کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اس میں ( سبب میں ) اور خواہ مصاہرت نکاح کی وجہ سے ہو یا زنا کی اصبح قول کے مطابق اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں (مفضی الی الحرج ہونے اور قلت رغبت
کی وجدت ) ۔ تشریح یہ محارم کو دیکھنے کی دلیل عقلی ہے کہ چونکہ ایسے رشتہ دار بغیر روک ٹوک کے ایک دوسرے کے گھر میں جاتے ہیں تو اگر ان مواضع کو دیکھنا حرام ہو جاتا تو حرج لازم آتا۔ نیز حرمت مؤبدہ کی وجہ سے رغبت کم ہوتی ہے البتہ ان کے علاوہ دیگر مواضع ، پیٹ، کمر، ران ان کو دیکھنا جائز نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ ان کے انکشاف کی عادت نہیں ہے نیز مواضع زینت کے علاوہ کی قرآن نے اجازت نہیں دی اور یہ مواضع زینت نہیں ہیں ( کمامر ) محرم وہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس مرد اور عورت کے درمیان کبھی نکاح جائز نہ ہو سکے خواہ رشتہ نسب کا ہو یا سب کا اور سبب سے مرادر ضاعت و مصاہرت ہے کیوں کہ یہاں بھی ضرورت ہے اور رغبت کی قلت ہے پھر مصاہرت نکاح کی وجہ سے قائم ہوگی یا زنا کی اسی دلیل سے۔ تنبیہ مصنف نے فی الاصح کی قید اس لئے کہ لگائی کہ اس میں بعض مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے انہوں نے فرمایا کہ زنا ہے ثابت ہونے والی مصاہرت کی وجہ سے دیکھنا اور چھونا جائز نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہاں مصاہرت کا ثبوت بطریق عقوبت ہے نہ کہ بطریق ہے نعمت اور
جب اس کی خیانت ایک مرتبہ ظاہر ہوگئی تو اس پر دوبارہ اعتماد نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے مگر اصح یہ ہے کہ اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ تنبیه - ۲ شامی ص ۲۳۵ ج ۵ پر بھی اس کو ترجیح دی گئی ہے والا ول اصبح اعتبار اللحقيقة لانها محرمة عليه على التابيد.
What parts of his mahram women a man may see and what he may not see. He said: A man looks from his mahram women at the face, head, chest, shins, and upper arms, and he does not look at her back, belly, and thigh. The source for this is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And let them not display their adornment except to their husbands...' and the meaning, and Allah knows best, is the places of adornment, and they are what we mentioned in the book. Included in that are the forearm, ear, neck, and foot, because these are places of adornment, unlike the back, belly, and thigh, because they are not places of adornment. Translation: Quduri said: And a man looks from his mahram women at the face, head, chest, shins, and arms, and does not look at her back, belly, and thigh. The source for this is the command of Allah Almighty: 'And let them not display their adornment except to their husbands...' and the meaning, and Allah knows best, is the places of adornment, and they are those which we have mentioned in the book. Included in that are the wrist, ear, neck, and foot, because these are places of adornment, unlike the back, belly, and thigh, because they are not places of adornment. Explanation: Women who are mahram by blood (dhi rahm) – a man may see their face, head, chest, shins, and arms, and he may not see their belly and back. Because in the mentioned verse, permission is given to display adornment to mahrams, and adornment means the places of adornment. And these are the same places mentioned, and included are the wrist, neck, ear, and foot, because these are all places of adornment, as it is customary to wear jewelry etc. on all these places. However, the waist, belly, and thigh are not places of adornment, so permission to display them has not been given. Rational proofs for looking at mahrams: And because some enter upon others without seeking permission and without shyness, and the woman is in her house usually in her work clothes. So if looking at these places were prohibited, it would lead to hardship. Similarly, desire decreases due to perpetual prohibition, so what is desired is little, unlike the parts beyond these (belly, back, thigh) because they are not usually uncovered. And a mahram is one between whom and the woman marriage is never permissible, whether due to lineage or due to a cause like fosterage and affinity, because both meanings (necessity and lack of desire) exist in it. And whether the affinity is through marriage or fornication – according to the most correct view – due to the proof we have mentioned. Translation: And because some enter upon others without permission and without modesty, and the woman is usually in her house in her work clothes. So if looking at these places were made unlawful, it would lead to hardship. Similarly, due to perpetual prohibition, desire decreases, so desire is little, unlike the parts beyond these (belly, back, thigh) because they are not usually uncovered. And a mahram is one between whom and that woman marriage is never permissible, whether due to lineage or due to a cause like fosterage and affinity, because both meanings (necessity and lack of desire) exist. And whether the affinity is through marriage or fornication – according to the most correct view – due to the same proof we have mentioned (leading to hardship and lack of desire). Explanation: This is a rational proof for looking at mahrams: since such relatives enter each other's homes without restriction, if looking at these parts were forbidden, it would cause hardship. Also, due to perpetual prohibition, desire decreases. However, other parts – belly, waist, thigh – looking at them is not permissible, because they are not usually uncovered, and the Qur'an did not permit other than the places of adornment. And these are not places of adornment. A mahram is one between whom and the woman marriage can never be valid, whether the relationship is by lineage or by cause, and cause refers to fosterage and affinity, because here too there is necessity and lack of desire. Then affinity is established either by marriage or by fornication – due to the same proof. Warning: The author added the condition 'according to the most correct view' because there is a difference of opinion among some scholars. They said that due to fornication, looking and touching would not be permissible because here the establishment of affinity is by way of punishment, not by way of blessing, and when her treachery has become evident once, she cannot be trusted again. But the most correct view is that there is no harm in it (it is permissible). Note 2: In Shami, vol. 5, p. 235, this view is also given preference, and the most correct is to consider the reality because she is perpetually forbidden to him.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding which body parts a man may see of his mahram women. The Hanafi position, based on al-Quduri's matn, is that a man may see the face, head, chest, shins, and upper arms. He may also see the forearm, ear, neck, and foot, as these are customary places of adornment. He may not see the back, belly, or thigh. The primary proof is Quran 24:31, which permits displaying adornment to mahrams; the places of adornment are those where jewelry is worn. A rational proof (istihsan) is added: since mahrams frequently interact in daily life without formality, prohibiting all looking would cause hardship. The text then defines a mahram as one with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, whether by lineage, fosterage, or affinity. It notes a dispute: does zina (fornication) create mahramiyyah? Some scholars say no, because affinity through zina is a punishment, not a blessing, and trust is lost. But the most correct (asahh) view in the Hanafi school is that zina also creates mahramiyyah, because the woman becomes perpetually forbidden to the man in marriage, based on the same cause of hardship and lack of desire. The commentary confirms this with reference to al-Shami.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, fosterage, or affinity (including zina per asahh).
زینت (zeenah): Adornment; in this context, the places where adornment is customarily worn (jewelry).
مصاہرت (musaharah): Affinity, a relationship created by marriage or, in the asahh view, by zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, which of the following is a prohibited part to see on a mahram woman?
A) Face
B) Head
C) Thigh
D) Chest

Key Takeaway
A man may see mahram women's customary places of adornment (face, head, chest, shins, arms) but not the back, belly, or thigh, based on Quran 24:31 and the principle of avoiding hardship.

Seclusion and Travel with Mahram
Ruling on seclusion and travel with mahram women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seclusion and travel with mahram women, cite the hadith proofs, and explain the wajh al-dalalah that permits them.

Core Idea
Seclusion and travel with a mahram are permissible; the prohibition is only for non-mahrams.

This lesson examines the permissibility of seclusion (khalwa) and travel with mahram women. The Hanafi school relies on two hadiths to establish that such actions are not prohibited. Understanding the exception for mahrams is key to applying these rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The acts are seclusion (khalwa) and travel with mahram women. The ruling is that there is no harm (la ba'sa), meaning it is permissible (mubah).
The term 'mahram' refers to a relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: the first prohibits a woman traveling more than three days except with her husband or a mahram; the second warns against khalwa with a woman who is not permissible (laysa minha bi-sabil).
The first hadith is in Muslim; the second in Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the first hadith, the exception (illa) for husband or mahram indicates that travel with them is not prohibited. In the second, the phrase 'laysa minha bi-sabil' is interpreted to mean a non-mahram, so the prohibition applies only to non-mahrams, implying khalwa with a mahram is allowed.
This interpretation relies on the linguistic implication of the exception.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While Hanafis permit khalwa with mahram, some other schools may restrict it if there is fear of fitna (temptation). This difference arises from varying degrees of caution.
Imam al-Shafi'i is reported to advise against khalwa even with mahram in certain circumstances.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school follows the apparent meaning (zahir) of the hadith and does not add extra restrictions. The mufta bihi position is permissibility.
This is based on the principle that the default ruling for acts is permissibility unless prohibited by a clear text.

Source Text

ولا باس بالخلوة والمسافرة بهن لقوله عليه السلام لا تسافر امرأة فوق ثلثة ايام ولياليها الا ومعها زوجها او ذو رحم محرم منها وقوله عليه السلام الالايخلون رجل بامراة ليس منها بسبيل فان ثالثهما الشيطان والمراد اذالم يكن محرما

ترجمہ اور کوئی حرج نہیں ہے محارم کے ساتھ خلوت میں اور مسافرت میں نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ سفر نہ کرے عورت تین دن اور تین رات سے زیادہ (یعنی مقدار مسافرت قصر کہ یہی شرعی سفر ہے مگر اس کے ساتھ اس کا شوہر یا اسکا ذ ورحم محرم ہو اور نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے آگاہ ہو جاؤ کوئی مرد خلوت نہیں کرتا کسی عورت کے ساتھ کہ اس کے ساتھ خلوت کی کوئی راہ نہیں ہے پس ان میں سے تیسرا شیطان ہوتا ہے اور مراد یہ ہے کہ جب کہ وہ محرم نہ ہو۔ تشریح اپنی محارم کے ساتھ سفر بھی جائز ہے اور خلوت بھی پہلی حدیث سے سفر کا جواز معلوم ہوا اور دوسری حدیث سے خلوت کا جواز معلوم ہوا اس لئے کہ یہاں لیس منها بسبیل سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جب وہ محرم نہ ہو لہذا اگر محرم ہوتو پھر یہ حکم نہیں ہے یعنی خلوت جائز ہے۔ پہلی حدیث مسلم میں ہے اور دوسری ترندی اور نسائی میں ہے۔
And there is no harm in seclusion and travel with them (mahram women) due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'A woman should not travel for more than three days and nights except with her husband or a mahram relative of hers.' And his saying: 'Beware: let no man seclude himself with a woman who is not permissible for him, for the third of them is Satan.' And the meaning is when he is not a mahram.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage rules on seclusion (khalwa) and travel with mahram women. The two hadiths cited are: (1) The hadith that a woman may not travel beyond the distance of qasr (three days travel) unless accompanied by her husband or a mahram. (2) The hadith that prohibits khalwa with a woman who is not permissible (i.e., a non-mahram). The commentary explains: Since the exception in the second hadith (laysa minha bi-sabil) refers to a non-mahram, it implies that khalwa with a mahram is permissible. Both hadiths are authentic; the first in Muslim, the second in Tirmidhi and Nasa'i.

Key Terms
خلوة (khalwa): Being alone with a woman in a place where no one else can enter.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim muhrim): A male relative who is a mahram (unmarriageable) through blood or milk kinship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She must have her husband or mahram with her
B) She must be over 40 years old
C) She must travel with a group of women
D) It is always prohibited

Key Takeaway
Seclusion and travel with mahram women are permissible in the Hanafi school based on the explicit exceptions in the hadith.

Looking at Another's Female Slave: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling on looking at another's female slave with illa and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on looking at another's female slave and identify the illa (reason) that permits it.

Core Idea
A man may look at another's slave girl as he looks at his mahram — her work necessity lightens the covering rules.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a unique Hanafi ruling on the awrah of a slave woman toward strangers. Unlike a free woman, a female slave frequently leaves the home for her master's tasks, making full covering impractical. The ruling analogizes her situation outside the home to that of a free woman inside the home before mahrams, establishing the permissible limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being looked at? What is the hukm (legal classification)? The act is looking at another person's female slave. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) for a man to look at her to the same extent as he looks at his own mahram women.
The ruling is explicit in the text: ينظر الرجل من مملوكة غيره الى ما يجوز ان ينظر اليه من ذوات محارمه
2
Determine the permissible parts
From the analogy to mahram, a man may look at her face, hands, and feet — the parts normally visible to mahram relatives.
Hanafi fiqh defines mahram awrah as face and hands (and feet for slaves).
3
Identify the illa (reason)
The author gives the cause: 'because she goes out for her master's needs and serves his guests, and she is in her work clothes.' This is an illa of necessity (ḥāja).
The term 'illa' is not explicit, but the phrase 'لانها تخرج' indicates the reasoning.
4
Recognize the analogy (tashbih)
Her situation outside the house with strangers is likened to a free woman inside the house with mahrams. This is a legal analogy: the ruling of looking at a mahram free woman is applied to a non-mahram slave woman.
The text: 'فصار حا لها خارج البيت في حق الاجانب كحال المراة داخله في حق المحارم'
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require a slave woman to cover like a free woman. The Hanafi school is more lenient due to the widespread need (umum al-balwa).
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; be aware of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وينظر الرجل من مملوكة غيره الى ما يجوز ان ينظر اليه من ذوات محارمه لانها تخرج لحوائج مولاها و تخدم اضیافه وهى فى ثياب مهنتها فصارحا لها خارج البيت فى حق الاجانب كحال المراة داخله في حق المحارم

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور دیکھے مرد اپنے غیر کی باندی سے اس حصہ کو جس کی جانب وہ دیکھ سکتا ہے اپنی محارم سے اس لئے کہ باندی نکلتی ہے اپنے مولیٰ کے حوائج کے لئے اور اس کے مہمانوں کی خدمت کرتی ہے اور وہ اپنے خدمت کے کپڑوں میں ہوتی ہے تو ہو گیا اس کا حال گھر سے باہر جانب کے حق میں جیسے عورت کا حال ہے گھر کے اندر محارم کے حق میں۔
He (al-Quduri) said: A man may look at another's female slave at what he is permitted to look at from his mahram women, because she goes out for her master's needs and serves his guests, and she is in her work clothes. So her situation outside the house, with respect to strangers, is like the situation of a woman inside the house with respect to mahrams.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on looking at a female slave belonging to another person. Al-Quduri states that a man may look at her as he would look at his own mahram (permissible parts). The reason ('illa) is that a slave woman frequently goes out for errands and serves guests, often wearing work clothes. Thus, her state outside the home is likened to a free woman inside the home in front of mahrams, meaning that covering is less strict. The Hanafi position is that one may look at her face, hands, and feet, similar to a mahram. This is based on the principle of necessity ('umum al-balwa).

Key Terms
مملوكة (mamlūka): A female slave owned by someone.
محارم (maḥārim): Unmarriageable relatives; here used as a standard for permissible looking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she is property
B) Because she goes out for work and serves guests, so necessity demands it
C) Because she is not Muslim
D) Because she is always covered

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits looking at another's female slave to the extent of mahram because her work necessitates it, and the ruling is based on her status, not her current attire.

Ruling on a Eunuch and Similar Individuals Looking at Non-Mahram Women
Rules that a eunuch and others with defects are still subject to the general prohibition of looking at non-mahram women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a eunuch looking at a non-mahram woman and identify the proofs used.

Core Idea
Castration or physical defect does not change male status for hijab; the general prohibition remains.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific question: are eunuchs and similar individuals exempt from the requirement of lowering the gaze? The author clarifies that they remain subject to the general prohibition, using a hadith from Aisha and resolving an apparent Quranic ambiguity by preferring the clear verse over the ambiguous one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals and the act
The passage mentions a eunuch (khasi), a man with severed penis (majbub), and a wicked effeminate man (mukhanath fasiq). The act in question is looking at a non-mahram woman.
All are considered males for hijab rulings.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that looking at non-mahram women is haram for all these individuals, just as it is for any normal man.
There is no exception due to physical defects.
3
Examine the first proof: Hadith of Aisha
The hadith states that castration (al-khisa') is a mutilation (muthla), so it does not make permissible what was previously forbidden. This indicates that a eunuch's status remains unchanged.
The hadith is considered gharib (weak) by some scholars, but the ruling is supported by other evidence.
4
Examine the second proof: Quranic verses and the rule of preferring muhkam over mutashabih
Surah Nur:30 is a clear verse (muhkam) commanding all believing men to lower their gaze. Surah Nur:31 is ambiguous (mutashabih) and may be interpreted to exempt some individuals. The Hanafi rule is that when clear and ambiguous conflict, the clear verse takes precedence, so the exemption does not apply.
This usul principle ensures the general application of the command.
5
Note the exception: young children
Young children who have not yet attained awareness of women's private parts are exempt by explicit text (Surah Nur:31).
This exception does not apply to adults with defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خصی کے لئے اجنبیہ کی طرف دیکھنے کا حکم
قال والخصى فى النظر الى الاجنبية كالفحل لقول عائشة رضى الله عنها الخصاء مثلة فلا يبيح ما كان حراما قبله ولانه فحل يجامع وكذا المجبوب لانه يسحق وينزل وكذا المخنث في الردى من الافعال لانه فحل فاسق والحاصل انه يوخذ فيه بمحكم كتاب الله المنزل فيه والطفل الصغير مستثنى بالنص

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور خصی اجنبیہ کی طرف دیکھنے میں نر کے مثل ہے عائشہ کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ خصی کرنا مثلہ کرنا ہے تو یہ (خصا) اس چیز کو مباح نہیں کرے گا جو اس سے (خصا سے پہلے) حرام تھی اور اس لئے کہ وہ ایسا نر ہے جو جماع کرتا ہے اور ایسے ہی مقطوع الذکر اس لئے کہ وہ رگڑتا ہے اور انزال کرتا ہے اور ایسے ہی بد کار مخنث اس لئے کہ وہ فاسق نر ہے اور حاصل یہ ہے کہ اس بارے میں اللہ تعالیٰ کی محکم کتاب کو لیا جائے گا جو اس بارہ میں نازل ہے اور چھوٹا بچہ نص کی وجہ سے مستثنی ہے۔ تشریح اجنبیہ کو دیکھنے میں نر کا حکم وہی خصی کا ہے حضرت عائشہ کا فرمان اس پر دال ہے کہ خصی ہونا یہ مثلہ کرنا ہے جو جائز نہیں لہذا اس فعل کی وجہ سے وہ چیز مباح نہیں ہو سکتی جو پہلے سے حرام ہے نیز خصی بھی نر ہے جماع کر سکتا ہے۔ اور یہی محبوب یعنی مقطوع الذکر کا حکم ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ابھی رگڑ رگڑ کر منی خارج کر سکتا ہے اور جو بد کار مخنث ہے یعنی بناوٹی وہ بھی نر کے حکم میں ہے البتہ یہ فاسق نر ہے۔ والحاصل ... الخ - اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ زیر بحث مسئلہ سے متعلق دو روایتیں ہیں
قل للمومنين يغضوا من أبصارهم ويحفظو افروجهم
۲ او التابعين غير اولى الاربة من الرجال
پہلی آیت محکم ہے جس میں عام مؤمنین کے لئے حکم ہے کہ وہ اپنی نظریں نیچی رکھیں اور دوسری آیت متشابہ ہے، جس میں تاویلات واقع ہوئی ہیں اور ایک تاویل سے یہ نکلتا ہے کہ مخنث ومحبوب اور خصی کے لئے بچوں کی طرح اجنبیہ کو دیکھنا جائز ہے لیکن یہ آیت چونکہ متشابہ ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جب محکم اور متشابہ میں تعارض ہو تو محکم کو ترجیح دی جائے گی لہذا ان سب کا یہی حکم کہ اجنبیہ کو دیکھنا حلال نہیں ہے بخلاف بچہ کے کہ اس کا استثناء نص میں موجود ہے فرمان باری ہے او الطفل الذين لم يظهروا على عورت النساء، وفيه تفصيل في العيني- تنبیہ حدیث عائشہ نہیں ملی علامہ زیلعی فرماتے ہیں قلت غریب نیز فرمایا ہے کہ مصنف کی دلیل کامیاب نہیں ہے ۔ ملاحظہ ہو نصب الرایہ ص ۲۵۰ ج ۴
Ruling for a eunuch regarding looking at a non-mahram woman. He said: The eunuch in looking at a non-mahram woman is like a normal man, due to the saying of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Castration is a mutilation, so it does not make permissible what was previously forbidden.' And because he is a male who copulates. Similarly, the one whose penis is cut off (majbub) because he rubs and emits semen. And similarly, the wicked effeminate man (mukhanath) because he is a sinful male. The conclusion is that in this matter, the clear book of Allah revealed on this topic is taken, and the young child is exempted by the text. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The eunuch in looking at a non-mahram woman is like a normal man, due to the saying of Aisha that castration is mutilation, so it does not make permissible what was previously forbidden. And because he is a male who copulates. Similarly, the one with severed penis because he rubs and emits. And similarly, the wicked effeminate man because he is a sinful male. The conclusion: In this matter, the clear book of Allah is taken, and the young child is exempted by the text. Explanation: The ruling for a non-mahram woman in looking is the same as for a eunuch. The hadith of Aisha indicates that castration is mutilation, which is not permissible, so that act cannot make permissible what was previously forbidden. Also, a eunuch is a male who can copulate. And the same applies to the majbub (penis severed) because he can still rub and emit semen. And the wicked mukhanath is also like a male, though a sinful one. The conclusion: There are two verses related to this issue: (1) 'Say to the believing men that they lower their gaze and guard their private parts' (Surah Nur:30), and (2) 'or those male attendants who have no need of women' (Surah Nur:31?). The first verse is clear (muhkam) and commands all believing men to lower their gaze. The second verse is ambiguous (mutashabih) and has interpretations; one interpretation exempts the mukhanath, majbub, and khasi, allowing them to look like children. But because the second is ambiguous, and the rule is that when clear and ambiguous conflict, the clear is preferred, so all of them are not allowed to look at non-mahram women, unlike children who are exempted by the text: 'or children who have not yet attained knowledge of women's private parts' (Surah Nur:31). There is detail in al-'Ayni. Caution: The hadith of Aisha is not found; 'Allama Zayla'i says: I say it is gharib. He also said that the author's proof is not sound. See Nasb al-Raya, vol.4, p.250.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage rules on individuals whose sexual capacity is altered: eunuchs (khasi), those with severed penis (majbub), and effeminate men (mukhanath). The Hanafi position is that they remain subject to the general prohibition of looking at non-mahram women, as castration or other changes do not alter their legal status as males. The proof is from Aisha's hadith that castration is mutilation and does not make permissible what was forbidden. Additionally, they are still capable of sexual activity (e.g., a eunuch can copulate, a majbub can rub and ejaculate). The commentary then resolves an apparent conflict between two Quranic verses: the clear verse (Surah Nur:30) commands all believing men to lower their gaze, while the ambiguous verse (Surah Nur:31, about 'those who have no need of women') might be interpreted to exempt such individuals. However, since the clear verse takes precedence, the exemption does not apply. The note at the end warns that the hadith of Aisha is weak (gharib), and the author's reliance on it may be questioned.

Key Terms
خصی (khasi): a eunuch, a castrated male
مجبوب (majbub): a man whose penis has been severed
مخنث (mukhanath): an effeminate man
محکم (muhkam): a clear, unambiguous verse
متشابہ (mutashabih): an ambiguous verse open to interpretation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a eunuch not allowed to look at non-mahram women?
A) Because he is not capable of intercourse
B) Because castration is a form of mutilation that does not change the ruling
C) Because the Quran specifically mentions eunuchs
D) Because he is considered a child

Key Takeaway
A eunuch and similar individuals are not exempt from hijab; they remain obligated to lower their gaze from non-mahram women.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
'Azl with a Free Wife vs. Slave Girl
States ruling with proof from Sunnah and rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'azl with a free wife versus a slave girl, and apply the distinction by identifying the underlying rationale (right to offspring).

Core Idea
With a free wife, 'azl requires her consent; with a slave girl, it does not — because the wife has a right to offspring.

The issue of 'azl (coitus interruptus) raises an important distinction in Hanafi fiqh based on the partner's legal status. While some may assume 'azl is always permissible, the school differentiates based on the woman's right to intercourse and offspring. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the rationale behind the difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage distinguishes between 'azl with one's own slave girl (amah) and with a free wife (hurrah). Note that the slave girl is owned by the man; if the wife is a slave belonging to another, the ruling is addressed elsewhere.
2
State the ruling for each
For the slave girl: 'azl is permissible without her permission. For the free wife: 'azl is NOT permissible without her permission. The Arabic uses 'la ya'zilu' indicating prohibition.
3
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The author cites a hadith: the Prophet forbade 'azl from a free woman except with her permission, and told the owner of a slave girl that he may do so if he wishes. Identify the explicit prohibition (nahy) and the permission (idhn).
The hadith is ahad, so zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for ruling.
4
Analyse the rationale (ta'lil)
The free wife has a right (haqq) to intercourse for fulfilling desire and obtaining offspring. This is supported by her choice to seek divorce if the husband is impotent or castrated. The slave girl has no such right; her purpose is service and enjoyment, so the master may prevent pregnancy without her consent.
This shows the ruling is based on the woman's legal entitlement, not merely on ownership.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih; other schools may permit 'azl without permission in both cases, or require permission in both. Note that the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the distinction as stated.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that a Hanafi husband must seek his wife's consent for 'azl, but not his slave girl's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويعزل عن امته بغير اذنها ولا يعزل عن زوجته الا باذنها لانه عليه السلام نهى عن العزل عن الحرة الا باذنها وقال لمولى امة اعزل عنها ان شئت ولان الوطئ حق الحرة قضاء للشهوة وتحصيلا للولد ولهذا تخير في الجب والعنة ولاحق للامة فى الوطئ فلهذا لا ينقص حق الحرة بغير اذنها ويستبد به المولى ولو كانت تحتة امة غيره فقد ذكرناها في النكاح ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور عزل کرے گا اپنی باندی سے بغیر اس کی اجازت کے، اور عزل نہیں کرے گا اپنی بیوی سے مگر اس کی اجازت سے، اس لئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے آزاد عورت سے عزل کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے مگر اس کی اجازت سے، اور باندی کے مولیٰ سے فرمایا کہ اگر تو چاہے تو اس سے عزل کر، اور اس لئے کہ وطی آزاد عورت کا حق ہے شہوت پوری کرنے اور اولاد حاصل کرنے کے لئے، اور اسی لئے وہ اختیار رکھتی ہے جب اور عننہ میں، اور باندی کا وطی میں کوئی حق نہیں، اس لئے آزاد عورت کا حق اس کی اجازت کے بغیر کم نہیں کیا جا سکتا، اور مالک اس میں خود مختار ہے۔ اور اگر اس کے نکاح میں دوسرے کی باندی ہو تو ہم نے اس کا ذکر نکاح میں کیا ہے۔
He said: And he may perform 'azl from his slave girl without her permission, and he may not perform 'azl from his wife except with her permission, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade 'azl from a free woman except with her permission, and he said to the owner of a slave girl: 'You may perform 'azl from her if you wish.' And because intercourse is a right of the free woman for fulfilling desire and obtaining offspring, and for this reason she has a choice in case of impotence and castration. And the slave girl has no right in intercourse, so the right of the free woman may not be diminished without her permission, and the owner may act independently in this matter. And if a man has under him a slave girl belonging to another, we have mentioned that in the book of Nikah. Translation: Quduri said: And he may perform 'azl from his slave girl without her permission, and he may not perform 'azl from his wife except with her permission, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade 'azl from a free woman except with her permission, and he said to the owner of a slave girl: 'If you wish, perform 'azl from her.' And because intercourse is a right of the free woman for fulfilling desire and obtaining offspring, and for this reason she has a choice in case of impotence and castration. And the slave girl has no right in intercourse, so the free woman's right may not be diminished without her permission, and the master is independent in this matter. And if he has under him a slave girl belonging to another, we have mentioned that in the book of Nikah.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on 'azl (coitus interruptus) with a slave girl versus a free wife. The ruling is clear: a man may practice 'azl with his own slave girl without her permission, but with his free wife, he must obtain her permission. The proof is from the Sunnah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade 'azl with a free woman except with her permission, while regarding a slave girl, he told her owner he could do it if he wished. The underlying rationale (ta'lil) is that the free wife has a right to sexual intercourse for both pleasure and procreation. She can seek divorce if her husband is impotent or castrated, indicating her right to offspring. The slave girl has no such right; her purpose is service and enjoyment, so the master may prevent pregnancy without her consent. This distinction is rooted in the difference in legal status: the free wife's rights are derived from the marriage contract, while the slave girl's rights are limited. The passage also notes a special case: if the wife is a slave belonging to another (i.e., she is married to a free man but owned by someone else), the ruling was already covered in the book of Nikah.

Key Terms
عزل (azl): Coitus interruptus, withdrawing before ejaculation to prevent pregnancy.
امة (amah): A female slave whom the man owns.
حرة (hurrah): A free woman, here specifically a wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, why is 'azl with a free wife prohibited without her permission?
A) Because she must bear children for her husband
B) Because intercourse is her right for fulfilling desire and obtaining offspring
C) Because the Prophet prohibited all forms of birth control
D) Because the slave girl has a higher status than a free wife

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'azl with a free wife requires her permission due to her right to offspring, while with a slave girl it is permissible without permission because she has no such right.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner

Ruling on 'Azl with Free Wife and Slave-Girl
Hanafi ruling with proof on 'azl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'azl with a free wife and a slave-girl, and identify the hadith evidence that supports each case.

Core Idea
With a free wife, 'azl needs her consent; with your slave-girl, you may do as you wish.

Intimate life in marriage involves mutual rights. Among them is the right to intercourse and procreation. The question of coitus interruptus ('azl) touches on these rights. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a free wife, who has a full right to intercourse, and a slave-girl, who does not. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parties
Recognize the two distinct scenarios: 'azl with one's free wife vs. 'azl with one's own slave-girl. The ruling differs based on the status of the woman.
Slave-girl here means a female slave owned by the man, not a wife who is a slave owned by another.
2
State the ruling for each
For the free wife: 'azl is impermissible without her permission. For the slave-girl: 'azl is permissible without her permission.
The permission of the wife is a condition for permissibility.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage cites two hadiths: one forbids 'azl with a free woman except with her consent; the other allows a master to perform 'azl with his slave-girl. Identify the source and implication.
The hadiths are narrated by Ibn Majah and Muslim respectively.
4
Understand the rationale
The free wife has a right to intercourse both for pleasure and childbearing; thus, 'azl diminishes her right. The slave-girl has no such right; therefore the master may act independently.
This rationale also explains why a free wife can seek annulment if the husband is impotent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويعزل عن امته بغير اذنها ولا يعزل عن زوجته الا باذنها لانه عليه السلام نهى عن العزل عن الحرة الا باذنها وقال لمولى امة اعزل عنها ان شئت ولان الوطى حق الحرة قضاء للشهوة وتحصيلا للولد ولهذا تخير في الجب والعنة ولاحق للامة فى الوطى فلهذا لا ينقص حق الحرة بغير اذنها ويستبد به المولى ولو كانت تحتة امة غيره فقد ذكرناها في النكاح
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور عزل کرے گا اپنی باندی سے بغیر اس کی اجازت کے اور عزل نہیں کرے گا اپنی بیوی سے مگر اس کی اجازت سے اس لئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے کرہ سے عزل کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے مگر اسکی اجازت سے اور باندی کے مولیٰ سے فرمایا کہ اگر تو چاہے تو اس سے عزل کر اور اس لئے کہ ولی حرق کا حق ہے شہوت کو پورا کرنے کیلئے اور بچہ کی تحصیل کے لئے اور اسی وجہ سے وہ اختیار دی جاتی ہے مجوب اور معینین کے بارے میں اور ولی میں باندی کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ پس اسی وجہ سے شوہر حرہ کے حق کو کم نہیں کر سکتا بغیر اس کی اجازت کے اور مولی اعزل کے ساتھ متفرد ہے اور اگر اس کے تحت اپنے غیر کی باندی ہو تو اس کو ہم نے کتاب النکاح میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح اپنی بیوی سے اگر عزل کرنا چاہتا ہے تو اس کی اجازت کے بغیر نہیں کر سکتا اور اپنی باندی سے بغیر اس کی اجازت کے عزل جائز ہے پہلی حدیث میں حرة سے عزل کی ممانعت ہے اور دوسری میں باندی سے عزل کی اجازت ہے۔
نیز باندی کا کوئی حق وطی میں نہیں ہے نہ اس کو مطالبہ وطی کا حق ہے لہذا پھر مولی ہی عزل کے بارے میں مستقل اور متفرد ہوگا اور آزاد عورت کا حق ہے اس لئے وہ وطی کا مطالبہ کر سکتی ہے قضاء شہوت کے لیے بھی اور تحصیل ولد کے لیے بھی تو جب اس کا حق ہے تو شوہر کو حق نہ ہوگا کہ اس کی اجازت کے بغیر اس کے حق میں نقصان کرے۔ ، آزاد عورت کے اس حق کی وجہ سے اس کو اختیار ملتا ہے جب کہ اس کا شوہر مقطوع الذکر یا عنین ہو باندی کے بارے میں گفتگو جب ہے کہ وہ اس کی باندی ہو ورنہ اگر دوسرے کی باندی سے نکاح کیا ہو تو مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کے حکم کو ہم کتاب النکاح میں بیان کر چکے ہیں دیکھئے ص ۳۲۲ ج ۲ تنبیہ حرة سے عزل والی حدیث کی تخریج ابن ماجہ نے کی ہے اور باندی سے عزل کی اجازت کی حدیث کی تخریج مسلم نے کی ہے۔ تفصیل کے لئے ملاحظہ ہو نصب الرایہ ص ۲۵ ج ۴
He said: And he may perform 'azl with his slave-girl without her permission, and he may not perform 'azl with his wife except with her permission, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade 'azl with a free woman except with her permission, and he said to the owner of a slave-girl: 'Perform 'azl with her if you wish.' And because intercourse is the right of the free woman for satisfying desire and obtaining children; for this reason she has the option in cases of impotence and eunuchs. And the slave-girl has no right to intercourse; so he does not diminish the right of the free woman without her permission, and the master is independent in regards to 'azl. And if he has a slave-girl belonging to someone else under him, we have mentioned it in the Book of Marriage. Translation: Quduri said: He may perform 'azl with his slave-girl without her permission, and he may not perform 'azl with his wife except with her permission, because the Prophet forbade 'azl with a free woman except with her permission, and he said to the owner of a slave-girl: 'If you wish, perform 'azl with her.' And because intercourse is the right of the free woman to satisfy desire and obtain children; for this reason she is given the choice regarding a eunuch or impotent man. And the slave-girl has no right to intercourse. Therefore, the husband cannot diminish the right of the free woman without her permission, and the master is independent regarding 'azl. And if under him is a slave-girl belonging to another, we have mentioned it in the Book of Marriage. Clarification: If he wishes to perform 'azl with his wife, he cannot do so without her permission; with his own slave-girl, 'azl is permissible without her permission. The first hadith prohibits 'azl with a free woman; the second permits it with a slave-girl. Also, the slave-girl has no right to intercourse, so the master is independent in 'azl. The free woman has the right to demand intercourse for desire and child; therefore, the husband cannot harm her right without permission. Due to this right, she has the option when her husband is impotent or a eunuch. The discussion about a slave-girl applies only if she is his own; if he marries another's slave-girl, the author says the ruling was given in the Book of Marriage. (See vol.2 p.322). Note: The hadith about 'azl with a free woman is narrated by Ibn Majah; the hadith permitting 'azl with a slave-girl is narrated by Muslim. For details, see Nasb al-Rayah vol.4 p.25.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on 'azl (coitus interruptus). The key distinction is between a free wife and a slave-girl. With a free wife, 'azl requires her permission because she has the right to intercourse for both pleasure and procreation. With one's own slave-girl, 'azl is permissible without permission because she has no such right. The proof comes from two hadiths: one forbidding 'azl with a free woman without her consent, and another allowing a master to perform 'azl with his slave-girl. The commentary explains that the free woman's right to intercourse gives her the legal capacity to seek annulment if the husband is impotent or a eunuch. The slave-girl has no similar right. If the slave-girl is owned by someone else but married to the man, the ruling differs and is covered in the Book of Marriage. The author also provides takhrij for the hadiths.

Key Terms
عزل (azl): Coitus interruptus; withdrawal before ejaculation to prevent pregnancy.
امہ (ummah): Female slave; slave-girl owned by the man.
حرة (ḥurrah): Free woman; a wife who is not a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when is 'azl (coitus interruptus) permissible without the partner's permission?
A) With both a free wife and a slave-girl.
B) Only with a free wife.
C) Only with one's own slave-girl.
D) With neither; permission is always required.

Key Takeaway
A free wife's right to intercourse makes 'azl conditional on her consent; a slave-girl lacks this right, so the master may act alone.
