Female Slave and Umm Walad Travel Without Mahram
Ruling on female slave and umm walad traveling without mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on travel for a female slave and umm walad without a mahram and explain the legal basis for the distinction from free women.

Core Idea
A female slave may travel without a mahram because strangers are legally like mahrams to her.

In classical Hanafi fiqh, the requirement of a mahram for travel applies differently to free women and female slaves. This lesson examines a clear ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that a female slave (amah) and an umm walad (slave who bore her master's child) may travel without a mahram. The reasoning hinges on the legal status of ownership: because a slave woman is owned, strangers are permitted to look at her in ways that would be unlawful for a free woman. This exception is well-established in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and remains the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the ruling applies specifically to a female slave (amah) and an umm walad (a slave who has borne her master's child). The text uses these two terms.
An umm walad is a type of female slave, but with the additional restriction that she cannot be sold.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that it is permissible (lā ba's) for them to travel without a mahram. The phrase lā ba's indicates no prohibition – it is mubāḥ.
This is a clear permission, not a recommendation or obligation.
3
Identify the legal basis
The text states: 'because strangers (ajānib) are in the position of mahrams with respect to female slaves in matters of looking and touching.' This is the key justification.
The earlier discussion referenced is about permissibility of looking at a slave woman; the same principle extends to travel.
4
Recognize the scope and limitation
This ruling applies only to female slaves, not to free Muslim women. Free women require a mahram for travel by consensus.
The distinction is based on ownership: a slave's body is legally accessible to her master, making strangers like mahrams.
5
Acknowledge the authority
The ruling is attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani and is part of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. It is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position with no known intra-Hanafi disagreement.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih: other schools require a mahram for all women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باندی اور ام ولد بغیر محرم کے سفر کر سکتی ہیں
قال ولا باس بان تسافر الامة وام الولد بغير محرم لان الاجانب فى حق الاماء فيما يرجع إلى النظر والمس بمنزلة المحارم على ما ذكرنا من قبل وام الولد ملك فيها وان امتنع بيعها والله اعلم بالصواب ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور کوئی حرج نہیں کہ باندی اورام ولد بغیر محرم کے سفر کریں اسلئے کہ اجانب باندیوں کے حق مین اس چیز میں جو کہ رائج ہے دیکھنے یا چھونے کی جانب محارم کے درجہ میں ہیں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم ما قبل میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور ام ولد ماندی ہے اس میں ملکیت کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اگر چہ اس کی بیع متنع ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تشریح ماقبل میں تفصیل گذر چکی ہے کہ باندی کی جانب دیکھنا اجانب کیلئے ایسا ہے جیسے اپنے محارم کی طرف دیکھنا لہذا باندی اور ام ولد بغیر محرم کے سفر کر سکتی ہیں۔ واللہ اعلم تم المجلد الأول من شرح المجلد الرابع من الهدايه يقوله تعالى و يتلوه المجلد الثاني اولة كتاب احياء الموات محمد یوسف غفر له التاو لوئی خادم التدریس دار العلوم و بو بند ۲۲ صفر ۱۴۱۱ھ
A female slave and an umm walad can travel without a mahram. He (Muhammad) said: There is no harm in a female slave and an umm walad traveling without a mahram, because strangers in respect of female slaves, regarding what is prevalent of looking and touching, are in the position of mahrams, as we mentioned before. And an umm walad is a slave with ownership established in her, even though her sale is prohibited. And Allah knows best. Translation: Muhammad said: There is no harm that a female slave and umm walad travel without a mahram, because strangers in the right of female slaves, in that which is prevalent, looking or touching, are in the grade of mahrams, according to the detail which we mentioned previously. And umm walad is a slave due to the establishment of ownership in her, even though her sale is prohibited. Allah knows best. Explanation: In the preceding section, the detail has passed that looking at a female slave by strangers is like looking at one's own mahrams. Therefore, a female slave and umm walad can travel without a mahram. Allah knows best. End of the first volume of the commentary on the fourth volume of al-Hidayah. He says (God's words) and the second volume follows. Beginning of the Book of Revitalizing Dead Lands. Muhammad Yusuf, may he be forgiven, from Tolawi. Teacher at Dar al-Ulum, and is bonded. 22 Safar 1411 AH.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Muhammad al-Shaybani (Imam Muhammad) stating that a female slave (amah) and an umm walad (a slave who has borne her master's child) may travel without a mahram (an unmarriageable guardian). The legal reasoning, referenced from an earlier discussion, is that for female slaves, strangers (ajānib) are treated like mahrams in matters of looking and touching. This is because a slave woman is owned by her master, and her body is legally accessible to him and, by extension, strangers are permitted to look at her in a way that would be impermissible for a free woman. This ruling applies even though an umm walad cannot be sold; she remains a slave with respect to ownership. Therefore, she can travel without a mahram. The passage ends with a colophon marking the end of the first volume of the commentary on the fourth volume of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
باندی (bāndī): A female slave (amah) in the context of travel rules.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, whose sale is prohibited but ownership remains.
محرم (mahram): An unmarriageable male relative (e.g., father, brother, son) with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, serving as a guardian for travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why can a female slave (amah) travel without a mahram?
A) Because she is free and independent.
B) Because strangers are like mahrams for her in looking and touching.
C) Because she is always accompanied by her master.
D) Because she has no need to travel.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a female slave and umm walad to travel without a mahram because the legal effect of ownership treats strangers as mahrams in matters of looking, touching, and travel.
